ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 6-1—6-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - HOSPITAL AUTHORITY 

Sec. 6-26. - Finding of need. 
It is hereby resolved by the authority of the commissioner of roads and revenues of the county that there is need for a hospital authority to function in the county under the provisions of the Hospital Authorities Law (O.C.G.A. § 31-7-70 et seq.). 
(Res. of 6-14-49, § 1) 
Sec. 6-27. - Created. 
There is created and constituted hereby a public body corporate and politic to be known as the Hospital Authority of Gordon County with all rights, powers, privileges and immunities provided for in the Hospital Authorities Law (O.C.G.A. § 31-7-70 et seq.). 
(Res. of 6-14-49, § 2) 
Sec. 6-28. - Composition. 
The hospital authority of the county shall consist of a board of trustees of five (5) members. 
(Res. of 6-14-49, § 3; Res. of 4-20-89) 
Sec. 6-29. - Residency requirement. 
The members of the hospital authority shall be residents of the county. 
(Res. of 4-20-89) 
Sec. 6-30. - Vacancies. 
All vacancies in the hospital authority board of trustees caused by death, removal from the county, resignation or otherwise shall be filled within thirty (30) days after vacancy occurs by election of the remaining members of the board of trustees. 
(Res. of 6-14-49, §§ 1A, 5) 
Sec. 6-31. - Selection and appointment of members; terms. 
(a)  In the process of appointments to fill vacancies on the hospital authority, commissioners nominating and authority members selecting persons to fill vacancies shall give consideration to the choice of a licensed doctor of medicine or a registered nurse to fill such vacancy, unless at the time of such appointment a licensed doctor of medicine or a registered nurse currently serves on the authority. 
(b)  Selection of a member to fill a vacancy on the authority shall be in accordance with the following procedure: 
(1)  The commissioners shall submit a list of three (3) eligible persons to the remaining members of the authority. 
(2)  The authority at its next regular meeting shall either select one (1) of the three (3) persons named in such list or decline to select any of the persons named in the list. If the authority declines to select any of the persons named on the list, it shall so notify the commissioners. 
(3)  If the authority declines to select any of the persons named on the list, the commissioners shall submit a second list of three (3) eligible persons, no one (1) of whom was named on the first list, to the authority. The authority, at its next regular meeting after receipt of the second list shall select one (1) of the three (3) persons named in the second list. 
(c)  Terms of office of the members shall be staggered as follows: The members shall be divided into three (3) classes with respect to the times for which they shall severally hold office. There shall be one (1) member of the first class who shall hold office until December 31, 1989. There shall be two (2) members of the second class who shall hold office until December 31, 1990. There shall be two (2) members of the third class who shall hold office until December 31, 1991. After the expiration of the initial term of office for members of each class, a member shall be appointed for a term of three (3) years. 
(Res. of 6-14-49, §§ 4, 6; Res. of 4-20-89) 
Sec. 6-32. - Relinquishing office. 
All hospital authority trustees shall hold office until their successors are elected and qualified. 
(Res. of 6-14-49, § 7) 
Sec. 6-33. - Oath of members. 
Each hospital authority trustee shall, before assuming the duties of his office, take an oath to well and faithfully perform the duties of the office. 
(Res. of 6-14-49, § 2A) 
Secs. 6-34—6-55. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - FOOD SERVICE ESTABLISHMENTS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Food service establishments, O.C.G.A. § 26-2-370 et seq.

(Ord. of 3-6-90(4), § 1-1) 
Sec. 6-57. - Adoption of state rules.

(Ord. of 3-6-90(4), § 1) 
Sec. 6-58. - Enforcement. 
(a)  Upon information being made known to the health officer or his designee, he shall cause a citation to be issued requiring the violator to appear before the judge of the magistrate court on a day and time certain, then and there to stand trial for violation of this article. 
(b)  Citations issued hereunder shall be pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-63 and shall be personally served upon the person accused. Each citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial. 
(c)  The county attorney is hereby authorized and directed to act as legal counsel for the health officer in any appeals from magistrate court to the superior court of the county regarding any violation of this article. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(4), § 1-4) 
Sec. 6-59. - Penalty. 
(a)  Any person violating the terms of this article or rules and regulations promulgated pursuant hereto shall be punished as provided in section 1-7. 
(b)  In addition to all other provisions of this article, any violation of this article is hereby deemed to be a continuing hazard and may be abated by an application for injunction in the superior court of the county or other court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(4), § 1-5)

ARTICLE V. - HEALTH HAZARDS 

Sec. 6-106. - Title. 
This article shall be known and may be cited as the "Health Hazard Ordinance" of the county. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-1) 
Sec. 6-107. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Health hazard means whatever is dangerous or detrimental to human life or health and whatever renders or tends to render soil, air, water or food impure or unwholesome. 
Health officer means the director of health of the county or his authorized representative. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-3) 
Sec. 6-108. - Purpose. 
The purpose of this article is to define specific types of health hazards in order to: 
(1)  Protect residents from annoyance and health hazards of certain aggravating circumstances; 
(2)  Delineate residents' responsibilities and prohibited acts in the community. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-2) 
Sec. 6-109. - Scope. 
Nothing in this article shall be interpreted or applied so as to create any power or duty in conflict with the preemptive effect of any federal or state law. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-4) 
Sec. 6-110. - Specific hazards enumerated. 
The following are specifically declared to be health hazards: 
(1)  Toilets, other sanitary facilities, plumbing or sewers not in compliance with the rules and regulations of the county board of health or the state department of human resources. 
(2)  Conditions conducive to the excessive breeding of rodents, flies, mosquitoes or other insects and vermin in relation to surrounding conditions as determined by the health officer. 
(3)  Pollution of the air by gases, vapors, fumes, mists, dust or smoke in quantities sufficient to be disagreeable, discomforting or detrimental to health or well-being in relation to the conditions of the surrounding area, as determined by the health officer. 
(4)  Trash, garbage, refuse or any foul, decaying or putrescent material kept in such quantities or used in such a manner or place as to be or become offensive, objectionable or detrimental to health or well-being. 
(5)  Keeping of horses, mules, asses, cows, sheep, goats, hogs, dogs, rabbits, guinea pigs, hamsters, chickens, turkeys, geese, ducks, pigeons or similar fowl or animals except under the following conditions: 
a.  Any housing or enclosures used by such animals or fowl shall be well drained, free from accumulations of animal excrement and objectionable odors, and otherwise clean and sanitary. Animal excrement shall be disposed of in a manner approved by the health officer. 
b.  Such animals or fowl shall be kept at the following minimum distances from any occupied building except the dwelling unit of the owner: 

 
Horses, mules, asses or cows ..... 75  
Sheep or goats ..... 75  
Hogs ..... 900  
Dogs ..... 25  
Rabbits, guinea pigs or hamsters ..... 25  
Chickens, turkeys, geese, ducks, pigeons or similar fowl ..... 25  
c.  All such animals or fowl, except dogs in areas where confinement of dogs under the rabies control regulations does not apply, shall be kept in adequate enclosures or tethered. 
d.  Diseased animals or fowl which might infect healthy animals or cause a menace to the public health shall be isolated or destroyed as the health officer deems necessary. 
e.  In the case of bona fide licensed pet shops, veterinary hospitals, stockyards, poultry houses and similar commercial establishments the health officer may modify these requirements where undue hardship would result from their strict enforcement. 
f.  Bona fide commercial agricultural enterprises are hereby exempt from the requirement of subsections (5)a., c. and d. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-5) 
Cross reference— Licenses and business regulations, Ch. 7; solid waste, Ch. 15. 
Sec. 6-111. - Creating, maintaining, etc., hazard prohibited. 
No person shall create, maintain, support, aid or continue a health hazard. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-6) 
Sec. 6-112. - Enforcement. 
(a)  Upon information being made known to the health officer that any violation of this article is occurring, he shall cause a citation to be issued requiring the violator to appear before the judge of the magistrate court on a day and time certain, then and there to stand trial for violation of this article. 
(b)  Citations issued hereunder shall be pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-63, and shall be personally served upon the person accused. Each citation shall state the time and place at which the accused is to appear for trial. 
(c)  The county attorney is hereby authorized and directed to act as counsel for the health officer in any appeals from the magistrate court to the superior court regarding any violation of this article. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-9) 
Sec. 6-113. - Penalty. 
(a)  Any person convicted of violating the terms of this article or rules and regulations promulgated pursuant hereto shall be punished as provided in section 1-7. 
(b)  In addition to all other provisions of this article, any violation of this article is hereby deemed to be a continuing hazard and may be abated by an application for injunction in the superior court of the county or other court of competent jurisdiction. 
(Ord. of 3-6-90(1), § 1-10) 
Secs. 6-114—6-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - SMOKING PROHIBITIONS[4] 

Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
Cross reference— Personnel, Ch. 10. 

Sec. 6-151. - Findings. 
(a)  The United States Surgeon General has stated that smoking of cigarettes and the use of tobacco products is the leading cause of premature death and disability in the United States of America. Medical evidence confirms that smoking of tobacco can be hazardous to the health of the smoker and nonsmoker. Medical research has confirmed that nonsmokers with chronic heart or lung disease can experience distress when exposed to sufficient concentrations of secondhand smoke. Many allergic individuals and healthy nonsmokers report discomfort when exposed to secondhand smoke. Recent medical studies provide sufficient evidence that long-term exposure to involuntary smoking may increase a nonsmoker's risk of developing serious lung disease. 
(b)  The board of commissioners finds that it is in the best interest of the health, welfare and safety of the county and its citizens: 
(1)  To provide a healthy, comfortable and productive working environment for its employees in the county's public buildings and facilities serving the public as well as in motor vehicles; 
(2)  To protect nonsmokers; 
(3)  To help employees to adjust to restrictions on smoking and the use of tobacco products; and 
(4)  To prohibit smoking of cigarettes and the use of other tobacco products in any county-owned or leased enclosed building space as well as in motor vehicle(s) occupied by at least one (1) nonsmoker. 
(Ord. of 4-26-94, § 1) 
Sec. 6-152. - Prohibitions. 
From the effective date of this article smoking of cigarettes or the use of other tobacco products by whatever name known or called now or in the future is prohibited in any enclosed building space as well as in any motor vehicle occupied by at least one (1) nonsmoker owned or leased by the county and any of its departments, agencies, boards, authorities and commissions. For purposes of this section, the term "nonsmoker" shall mean any individual who declares that he/she does not smoke cigarettes or other tobacco products or has discontinued the smoking of cigarettes or other tobacco products. 
(Ord. of 4-26-94, § 2) 
Sec. 6-153. - Conflict with other regulations. 
The provision of section 6-152 will in no instance conflict with any existing or future regulation(s) established for fire, health or safety reasons. 
(Ord. of 4-26-94, § 3) 
Sec. 6-154. - Implementation. 
The board of commissioners is authorized and directed to promulgate and disseminate to all employees of the county the findings contained in this article and to provide for its implementation as follows: 
(1)  All departments, agencies, authorities, boards, commissions and elected officers will give this article wide dissemination to all employees; 
(2)  All prospective new county employees will be informed of this no-smoking and no-use of tobacco products policy before they are hired; and 
(3)  Signs will be placed in all appropriate spaces and county buildings indicating that smoking and the use of tobacco products are not allowed, with such signs to be uniform in language and color. 
(Ord. of 4-26-94, § 4) 
Sec. 6-155. - Employee responsibility. 
All employees of the county share in the responsibility for adhering to and enforcing this policy. 
(Ord. of 4-26-94, § 5) 
Sec. 6-156. - Violations; penalties. 
(a)  (1)    ;hg;Any violations of section 6-152 or conflict concerning its implementation should be brought to the attention of appropriate supervisory personnel. In all cases the right of a nonsmoker to protect his or her health and comfort will take precedence over an employee's or nonemployee's desire to smoke or use tobacco products. 
(2)  Violations of this article by an employee may be subject to appropriate disciplinary action under the provisions of the county personnel ordinance [Chapter 10 of this Code], now in effect or as amended hereinafter. 
(b)  Any nonemployee of the county who continues to violate the provisions of section 6-152 after receiving an oral request to cease smoking of the cigarette or use of tobacco material from authorized personnel with offices located in the enclosed building or having responsibility for the motor vehicle shall be subject to citation to the magistrate court of the county and upon adjudication of guilt may be fined not less than twenty-five dollars ($25.00) per violation. The board of commissioners in implementing the provisions of this article shall designate authorized personnel in each department to make such oral requests as provided in this subsection. 
(Ord. of 4-26-94, § 6) 
Secs. 6-157—6-180. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - PRODUCTS USED IN THE PREPARATION OF METHAMPHETAMINE 

Sec. 6-181. - Definitions. 
Product used in the preparation of methamphetamine: Any compound, mixture, preparation or drug product containing any detectable quantity of ephedrine, pseudoephedrine or phenylpropanolamine, or any of their salts, isomers or salts of isomers, alone or in a mixture. 
(Ord. of 12-7-04, § 1) 
Sec. 6-182. - Display of products prohibited. 
Products used in the preparation of methamphetamine may not be openly displayed for sale in the unincorporated area of the county, but must be maintained behind the counter and distributed for sale only by the pharmacist, pharmacy technician, sales clerk or other retail distributor employee. 
(Ord. of 12-7-04, § 2) 
Sec. 6-183. - Requirements for purchase of products. 
Products used in the preparation of methamphetamine may not be dispensed, sold or distributed in the unincorporated area of the county without requiring the individual purchasing, receiving or otherwise acquiring such compound, mixture, preparation or drug product to produce a photo identification showing their date of birth and sign a written log or receipt showing their signature and printed name, the date of the transaction, the type and amount of product purchased. 
The log or receipt must be maintained by the retailer or other person dispensing, selling or distributing the drug used in preparation of methamphetamine for a period of three (3) years. 
The log shall contain at a minimum the following information: 
(1)  The specific quantity of the products used in the preparation of methamphetamine purchased; 
(2)  Signature of the purchaser; 
(3)  The name and residential or mailing address of the purchaser (other than a post office box); 
(4)  The number of the purchaser's motor vehicle operator's license or other proper identification used at the time of the purchase; 
(5)  The date of such purchase; and 
(6)  The signature of an employee of the retail establishment as witness to the purchase and identification of the purchaser. 
In addition, the retailer or other person dispensing, selling or distributing the drug used in the preparation of methamphetamine shall also include in the log a monthly total listing the amount of such compound, mixture, preparation or drug product which was purchased for sale in their establishment. 
(Ord. of 12-7-04, § 3) 
Sec. 6-184. - Violations and enforcement. 
(a)  Violations of this article shall be considered a misdemeanor punished in accordance with O.C.G.A. §§ 15-10-60 et seq. and 36-1-20 and the Gordon County Code of Ordinances. 
(b)  The provisions of this article shall be enforced by the Calhoun/Gordon County Drug Task Force, the Gordon County Sheriff's Office, the Gordon County Ordinance Officer, and any other designated party. 
(Ord. of 12-7-04, § 4) 
Chapter 7 - LICENSES AND BUSINESS REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes:

Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, Ch. 3; buildings, Ch. 4; health, Ch. 6; motor vehicles and traffic, Ch. 8; signs, Ch. 13; soil erosion and sedimentation, Ch. 14; solid waste, Ch. 15; taxation, Ch. 16; specific health hazards, § 6-110; zoning, Ch. 18.

Tit. 10; business and occupational license taxes and fees, O.C.G.A. § 36-1-22; certain persons prohibited from investigating business for issuance of county license, O.C.G.A. § 36-60-9; professions and businesses, O.C.G.A. Tit. 43; specific, business, and occupation taxes, O.C.G.A. § 48-13-1 et seq.; registration and licensing of persons transporting motor vehicles and mobile homes, O.C.G.A. § 40-2-36. 

ARTICLE I. - BUSINESS LICENSE ORDINANCE 

Sec. 7-1. - Business license required. 
For the year 2001 and succeeding years thereafter, each person engaged in any business, trade, profession, or occupation in the unincorporated areas of Gordon County, Georgia, shall pay a regulatory fee and shall be issued a business license for said business, trade, profession, or occupation; which license and any applicable registration shall be displayed in a conspicuous place in the place of business, if the taxpayer has permanent business location in Gordon County, Georgia. If the taxpayer has no permanent business location in Gordon County, Georgia, such business registration shall be shown to the licensing official or representatives thereof, or to any law enforcement officer of said Gordon County upon request. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 1A) 
Sec. 7-2. - Construction of terms; definitions. 
(a)  Wherever the term "Gordon County" is used herein, such term shall be construed to mean Gordon County, Georgia; wherever the term "county" is used herein, it shall be construed to mean Gordon County, Georgia. Wherever the term "business" is used herein such term shall be construed to mean a business, trade, profession or occupation or practitioner thereof unless otherwise indicated. 
(b)  As used in this article, the term: 
(1)  Business license means a license issued following a registration with and fee paid to Gordon County prior to conducting or transacting business within the unincorporated areas of Gordon County. For the purposes of this article, the term "business license" shall be a type of "regulatory fees." 
(2)  Occupation tax means a tax levied on persons, partnerships, corporations, or other entities for engaging in an occupation, profession, or business for revenue raising purposes. 
(3)  Regulatory fees means payments, whether designated as license fees, permit fees, or by another name, which are required by a local government as an exercise of its police power and as a part of or an aid to regulation of an occupation, profession, or business. The amount of a regulatory fee shall approximate the reasonable cost of the actual regulatory activity performed by the county. A regulatory fee may not include an administrative fee. Regulatory fees do not include development impact fees as defined by paragraph 8 of O.C.G.A. § 36-71-2 or other costs or conditions of zoning or land development. 
(4)  Person shall be held to include sole proprietors, corporations, partnerships, nonprofit, or any other form of business organization, but specifically excludes charitable nonprofit organizations. 
(5)  Practitioner of profession or occupation is the one who by state law requires state licensure regulating such profession or occupation, but shall not include a practitioner who is an employee of a business, if the business pays a regulatory fee. 
(6)  Clerk means the Clerk of the Board of Commissioners of Gordon County. 
(7)  Licensing official means the county administrator or his designee. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 2) 
Sec. 7-3. - Regulatory fee structure. 
(a)  A regulatory fee may be imposed as provided under O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9 on applicable businesses, trades, professions and occupations. 
(b)  The regulatory fee schedule or schedules for persons in businesses, trades, professions, and occupations as set forth in O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9 or other provisions of Georgia law shall be adopted by the Gordon County Board of Commissioners and shall be amended from time to time. Said regulatory fee schedule shall be posted in the Gordon County Administration Office and at the building, planning and development office. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 3) 
Sec. 7-4. - Purpose and scope of fee. 
This article is adopted pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. §§ 48-13-8 and 48-13-9 and is for regulatory purposes only. This article is not adopted as an occupational tax. 
(1)  No business or practitioner shall be required to pay more than one regulatory fee for each of its locations. 
(2)  A business with multiple locations in the county will not be assessed more than two hundred dollars ($200.00) for their business license for all their locations combined. 
(3)  No business license or regulatory fee shall be required for those businesses and practitioners of professions or occupations which Gordon County is not authorized to subject to regulatory fees pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-13-9(c). 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 4A) 
Sec. 7-5. - Paying regulatory fee of business with no location in Gordon County, Georgia. 
A business license shall also be required on those businesses, trades and practitioners of professions or occupations which operate and conduct business within Gordon County even if said business, trade, profession or occupation does not have a location within Gordon County. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 5A) 
Sec. 7-6. - Each line of business to be identified on business registration. 
As part of the application process of obtaining a business license, each business operated within the unincorporated areas of Gordon County shall register said business with Gordon County. The business registration of each business operated within the unincorporated areas of Gordon County shall identify the line or lines of business that the business conducts. No business shall conduct any line of business without first having that line of business registered with the county and that line of business being noted by the county upon the business registration form which is to be displayed by the business owner. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 6) 
Sec. 7-7. - The number of businesses considered to be operating in the county. 
Where a person conducts business at more than one (1) fixed location, each location or place shall be considered a separate business for the purpose of this article. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 7) 
Sec. 7-8. - Imposition of fee. 
The regulatory fee imposed herein is for regulatory purposes only. Said fee shall be paid before commencing a business, trade or the practice of a profession or occupation as a condition precedent for transacting business or practicing a profession. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 8) 
Sec. 7-9. - When fee due and payable; effect of transacting business when fee delinquent. 
(a)  Each such regulatory fee shall be for the calendar year 2001 and succeeding calendar years thereafter unless otherwise specifically provided. Said registration and fee shall be payable before commencing business and thereafter on January 1 of each year once the business has commenced and has received its initial license, and be subject to penalties for delinquency as prescribed in this article. Should any regulatory fee imposed by this article remain due and unpaid for ninety (90) days from the due date of the fee, unless otherwise exempted by state law or local ordinance, the person liable for the fee shall be subject to and shall pay a penalty of ten (10) percent of the fee due. In addition, interest on the regulatory fee due and payable after the due date shall be at the rate of one five-tenths (1.5) percent per month. 
(b)  The regulatory fee herein provided for shall be issued by the licensing official and if any person, firm, or corporation whose duty it is to obtain a business license shall, after said fee becomes delinquent, transact or offer to transact, in the county, any trade or calling subject to this article without having first obtained said registration, such offender shall, upon conviction, be punished by a fine not to exceed five hundred dollars ($500.00). Payment of such fine may be enforced by the contempt powers of the court having competent jurisdiction. This remedy is in addition to any other remedies available for the collection of regulatory fees due to Gordon County from persons subject to the fee who fail or refuse to pay the fee. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 9) 
Sec. 7-10. - Exemption on grounds that business is operated for charitable purpose. 
No business on which a business license is imposed by this article shall be exempt from said license requirement on the ground that such business is operated for a charitable purpose, unless said business is registered as a nonprofit organization pursuant to the Internal Revenue Code. In such case, said business shall only be required to register with Gordon County and the fee shall be waived. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 10) 
Sec. 7-11. - Evidence of state registration required if applicable; state registration to be displayed. 
(a)  Each person who is licensed by the Secretary of State pursuant to O.C.G.A. title 43 shall provide evidence of proper and current state licensure before the county registration may be issued. 
(b)  Each person who is licensed by the state shall post the state license in a conspicuous place in the licensee's place of business and shall keep the license there at all times while the license remains valid. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 11) 
Sec. 7-12. - Evidence of qualification required if applicable. 
Any business required to obtain health permits, bonds, certificates of qualification, certificates of competency, or any other regulatory matter shall first, before the issuance of a county business license, show evidence that such requirements have been met. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 12) 
Sec. 7-13. - Liability of officers and agents; registration required; failure to obtain. 
Every person commencing business in the county after January 1 of each year shall likewise obtain the business license and registration herein provided for before commencing the same; and any person transacting, or offering to transact in the county, any business, trade, profession, or occupation required to be registered without first having so obtained said registration, shall be subject to penalties provided therefor. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 13) 
Sec. 7-14. - When registration and fee due and payable; effect of transacting business when fee delinquent. 
(a)  Each such registration shall be for the calendar year in which the registration was obtained unless otherwise specifically provided. There is hereby imposed a penalty upon each business which fails to apply for and obtain an appropriate business registration and pay all fees as provided herein before January 31 of each year, and on January 31 each year hereafter. Every person commencing business in the county after January 1 of each year shall obtain the registration required before commencing such business. Any person transacting or offering to transact in the county any business, trade, profession, or occupation without first having obtained said registration shall be subject to the penalties provided in section 7-15. Said penalties shall be in addition to all other penalties herein provided. 
(b)  The registration herein provided for shall be issued by the licensing official, and if any person, firm or corporation whose duty it is to obtain a registration shall, after said fee becomes delinquent, transact or offer to transact, in the county, any of the kind of business, trade, profession, or occupation without having first obtained said registration, such offender shall be subject to the penalties provided therefor. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 14) 
Sec. 7-15. - Penalty of ordinance violation. 
Any person violating any provision of this article shall, upon conviction, be fined in an amount not exceeding five hundred dollars ($500.00) per violation in the discretion of the Magistrate Court of Gordon County, and may be subject to any and all additional remedies available by law for the collection of regulatory fees. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 15) 
Sec. 7-16. - Businesses not covered by this article. 
(a)  The following businesses are not covered by the provisions of this article but may be assessed a regulatory fee, registration fee, or other type of regulation pursuant to the provisions of other general laws of the State of Georgia or by local law: 
(1)  Those businesses regulated by the Georgia Public Service Commission. 
(2)  Those electrical service businesses organized under chapter 3 of O.C.G.A. title 46. 
(3)  Any farm operation for the production from or on the land of agricultural products, but not including agribusiness. 
(4)  Cooperative marketing associations governed by O.C.G.A. § 2-10-105. 
(5)  Insurance companies governed by O.C.G.A. § 33-3-8 et seq. 
(6)  Motor common carriers governed by O.C.G.A. § 46-7-15. 
(7)  Those businesses governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-5-355. 
(8)  Agricultural products and livestock raised in the State of Georgia governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-5-356. 
(9)  Depository financial institutions governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93. 
(10)  Facilities operated by a charitable trust governed by O.C.G.A. § 48-13-55. 
(b)  The following persons or businesses are exempted from the regulatory fee imposed by this article: 
(1)  Nonprofit social, charitable, religious or fraternal organizations for the purpose of operating fairs, circuses or carnivals for periods of time not to exceed one (1) week. 
(2)  Individual farmers who raise, grow or cultivate edible food from the soil of the state provided, however, that farm, milk or other farmer cooperatives are not exempted when they engage in selling goods and/or services to the public in competition with persons taxed by virtue of this article. 
(3)  Established churches, religious, charitable and fraternal organizations chartered or operated for nonprofit purposes. 
(4)  Persons exempted from taxation by virtue of the constitution or any statute of the United States or State of Georgia. Such persons shall possess and display at their places of business a certificate of exemption that may be obtained from the licensing official by application of a form provided by the same. The applicant for exemption shall clearly state the provision of this article or other provision of law under which the applicant claims exemption. The certificate shall contain sufficient facts for the licensing official to determine whether the applicant is entitled to the exemption. The certificate of exemption shall remain valid and the business need not reapply for an annual certificate of exemption so long as the conditions entitling the business to the exemption remain the same. The application for the certificate of exemption shall be made under oath. The certificate of exemption shall not exempt any business from complying with the duty to register. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 16) 
Sec. 7-17. - Amendment, repeal of provision. 
This article shall be subject to amendment or repeal, in whole or in part, at any time. Said amendment may increase or lower the fee rates, and said amendments to the fee schedule shall be posted as provided in section 7-3 above. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 17) 
Sec. 7-18. - Applications of provisions to prior ordinance. 
This article does not repeal or affect the force of any part of any ordinance heretofore adopted where fees imposed under such prior ordinance have not been paid in full. So much and such parts of any ordinance heretofore and hereinafter passed as provided for the failure to pay regulatory fees provided for in said ordinance or ordinances, or failure to comply with any other provisions hereof, shall continue and remain in force until such regulatory fee, registration fee or assessment shall be fully paid. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 18) 
Sec. 7-19. - Enforcement of provisions. 
It is hereby made the duty of the licensing official to see that the provisions of this article relating to business licenses are observed; and to summon all violators of the same to appear before the court of competent jurisdiction. It is hereby made the further duty of the licensing official to inspect all registrations issued by the county, as often, as in his or her judgment, he or she may deem necessary to determine whether the registration held is the proper one for the business sought to be transacted thereunder. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 19) 
Sec. 7-20. - Provisions to remain in full force and effect until changed by governing body. 
This article shall remain in full force and effect until changed by amendment adopted by the Gordon County Board of Commissioners. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 20) 
Sec. 7-21. - Conflicts between specific and general provisions. 
Where there is an apparent conflict in this article between specific and general provisions, it is the intention hereof that the specific shall control. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 21) 
Sec. 7-22. - Conditions of issuance. 
The licensing official shall issue the certificate of license only: 
(1)  When satisfied that the business, etc., does not, and will not violate the requirements of the zoning ordinance of the county; 
(2)  Upon the fulfillment of the registration requirements of this article; and 
(3)  Upon the payment of the regulatory fee imposed by the ordinance. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 22) 
Sec. 7-23. - Term of certificate or license; transfer. 
Licenses will be issued for a one-year period, except as otherwise herein specified. A license issued by the licensing official under the authority of this article, may be transferred or assigned, except as otherwise noted in this article, provided the person conducts the business for which the license was issued at the same place and pays Gordon County a transfer fee of ten dollars ($10.00). If the business is moved to a different location, with the same owner and operators, the license may also be transferred to the new location, by notifying the licensing official and payment of the transfer fee. In the event that the proper authorities are not notified, an additional ten (10) percent fee shall be charged for the transfer. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 23) 
Sec. 7-24. - Misrepresentation-deemed violation. 
No person shall use any deceitful means or misrepresentation in obtaining the license or certificate to do business in the county from Gordon County. 
(Ord. of 2-22-2000, § 24) 
Sec. 7-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DEPOSITORY FINANCIAL INSTITUTIONS 

Sec. 7-26. - Annual tax levied. 
In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93, there is hereby levied an annual business license tax upon all depository financial institutions located within the county at a rate of 0.25 percent of the gross receipts of such depository financial institutions. Gross receipts shall mean gross receipts as defined in O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93. Depository financial institutions shall mean state and national banks, state building and loan associations, and federal savings and loan associations. 
(Res. of 5-6-86, § 1) 
Sec. 7-27. - Minimum tax. 
The minimum annual amount of business license tax due from any depository financial institution pursuant to this article shall be one thousand dollars ($1,000.00). 
(Res. of 5-6-86, § 2) 
Sec. 7-28. - Filing of return. 
Pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93(c), each depository financial institution subject to the tax imposed by this article shall file a return of its gross receipts with the board of commissioners by March 1 of the year following the year in which such gross receipts are measured. The return shall be in the manner and in the form prescribed by the state revenue commissioner based on the allocation method set forth in O.C.G.A. § 48-6-93(d). The board of commissioners shall assess and collect the tax levied pursuant to this article based upon the information provided in the return. 
(Res. of 5-6-86, § 3) 
Sec. 7-29. - Due date of taxes. 
Taxes levied pursuant to this article shall be due no later than thirty (30) days after filing of the return prescribed by section 7-28 unless extended by the board of commissioners. 
(Res. of 5-6-86, § 4) 
Secs. 7-30—7-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - COMMUNITY ANTENNA TELEVISION SYSTEMS[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Regulation of cable television systems, O.C.G.A. § 36-18-1 et seq. 

Sec. 7-51. - Short title. 
This article shall be known and may be cited as the "Gordon County Community Antenna Television Franchise Ordinance." 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 1) 
Sec. 7-52. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Applicant means any person or company authorized to do business in the state submitting an application for a community antenna television system in the county or who operates a CATV franchise in the county as of the effective date of this article. 
CATV franchise means a community antenna television system franchise. 
FCC means the Federal Communications Commission. 
Gross subscriber revenues means all revenue derived directly or indirectly from all sources by a selected applicant(s) from its CATV system within the unincorporated areas of the county before any deductions or expenses whatsoever. Definition of gross subscriber revenues shall be expanded as may be allowed by future FCC rulings. 
System means the lines, fixtures, equipment, attachments and all appurtenances thereto which are used in construction, operation and maintenance of a community antenna television system. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 2) 
Sec. 7-53. - Nonexclusive franchise. 
Each CATV franchise shall be nonexclusive, and the county may grant more than one (1) franchise for the unincorporated areas of the county. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 3) 
Sec. 7-54. - Application for franchise. 
(a)  No CATV franchise shall be granted until the following conditions are met: 
(1)  Notice shall be given to the board of commissioners of the intent of the applicant to apply for a CATV franchise. 
(2)  All applications for a CATV franchise shall be in a form acceptable to the board which provides the information required herein. 
(3)  All applications for a CATV franchise must be approved by the board. 
(4)  If the applicant is not a corporation, its application shall contain the names and addresses of persons (including corporations) having a proprietary or equitable interest in its business operation and/or proposed CATV franchise sought by the applicant. The term "equitable interest" shall include all assignments for value, as well as all contingent assignments of any right or privilege under the proposed CATV franchise, and shall also include any benefit, payment or emolument whatsoever resulting from the grant of a CATV franchise. 
(5)  If the applicant is a corporation not publicly held, as defined by the rules and regulations of the United States Securities and Exchange Commission, the statement shall furnish, additionally, the names and addresses of its officers, directors and shareholders, together with the number of shares held by each shareholder. 
(6)  If the applicant is a corporation publicly held, as defined by the rules and regulations of the United States Securities and Exchange Commission, the statement shall contain the states in which the applicant is incorporated and/or qualified to do business and the names and addresses of its officers and directors. 
(7)  The form of ownership of the facilities to be used in exercising the proposed CATV franchise. 
(8)  Any cable television system currently owned or operated by the applicant, its experience in operating and constructing such systems, any applications pending for other systems, and the general financial resources of the applicant as well as those specifically available for construction and operation of the proposed CATV system. 
(9)  Proposed services, including channel capacity, the number of channels to be included in basic services, the number of channels and types of services to be included in additional services, the number of two-way channels, the number of access channels and automated channels, facilities for local origination and a list of any additional services or facilities to be made available to the county and other public, institutional and community organizations. 
(10)  A schedule of the subscriber rates for each of the proposed services. 
(11)  The equipment to be included in the CATV system, the general routes of the feeder or trunk cable, the number and location of signal amplifiers to be used in redistributing signals, the proposed franchise area and the service schedule for the proposed franchise area. 
(12)  The design and construction plans and standards to be used in constructing or renovating the CATV system and the proposed construction and service schedule. 
(b)  All applications shall be open to public inspection during regular business hours. 
(c)  Any material misrepresentation in an application or the omission of any material representation, which omission renders the included representations misleading, whether done negligently or intentionally, shall be grounds for rejection of the application or termination of any CATV franchise granted on the basis of such application. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 4) 
Sec. 7-55. - Selection of applicants for negotiation. 
The board of commissioners shall hold a public hearing to review the applications submitted under this article and after considering the applicant's character, financial, technical and other qualifications and the adequacy and feasibility of its construction arrangements, the board may negotiate with the applicant for the purpose of granting a nonexclusive CATV franchise. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 5) 
Sec. 7-56. - Negotiation of proposed franchise. 
Upon selection, the board of commissioners and the selected applicant shall proceed to negotiate and draft the terms and conditions of a CATV franchise which shall contain the minimum terms and conditions set out in the remainder of this article (provided a franchise is granted to the selected applicant). 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6) 
Sec. 7-57. - Compliance with laws and regulations. 
The selected applicant shall at all times during the life of this franchise be subject to all lawful exercise of the police power by the county and to such reasonable regulation as the county shall by ordinance provide. The construction, operation and maintenance of the system by the selected applicant shall be in full compliance with the National Electrical Code as from time to time amended and revised, and in full compliance with all other applicable rules and regulations now in effect or hereinafter adopted by the Federal Communications Commission, the county, the state and the United States government. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(I)) 
Sec. 7-58. - Liability and indemnification. 
(a)  Liability coverage. It is expressly understood and agreed by and between the selected applicant and the county that the selected applicant shall save the county harmless from all loss sustained by the county on account of any suit, judgment, execution, claim or demand whatsoever arising out of the construction, operation and maintenance of the CATV system by the selected applicant. The selected applicant agrees to maintain and keep in full force and effect at all times during the term of the franchise sufficient liability insurance coverage to protect the county against any such claims, suits, judgments, executions or demands in a sum not less than five hundred thousand dollars ($500,000.00) per person in any one (1) claim, one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) as to any one (1) accident or occurrence, and not less than one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) for property damage as to any one (1) accident or occurrence, or in such larger sums on all coverage as may be required of the selected applicant by any other public utility in the county and shall provide the county with proof of such insurance. 
(b)  Workers' compensation coverage. The selected applicant shall also maintain in full force and effect throughout the duration of its franchise sufficient workers' compensation insurance coverage to adequately and fully protect its agents and employees as required by law. 
(c)  Resident company and agent. All insurance policies and bonds as are required by this section shall be written by a company or companies authorized and qualified to do business in the state. Certificates of all coverage required shall be promptly filed by the selected applicant with the county. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(II)) 
Sec. 7-59. - Conditions on street occupancy, system construction. 
(a)  Use. All transmission and distribution structures, lines and equipment erected by the selected applicant within the county shall be so located as to cause minimum interference with the proper use of streets, alleys and other public ways and places and to cause minimum interference with the rights or reasonable convenience of property owners who adjoin any of such streets, alleys or other public ways and places. 
(b)  Restoration. In case of any disturbance of pavement, sidewalks, driveways or other surfacing, the selected applicant shall have prior approval of the board of commissioners and shall, at its own expense and in a manner approved by the county, replace and restore such places so disturbed in as good condition as before the work commenced, and shall maintain the restoration in a condition approved by the county for the full period of one (1) year; and if the selected applicant fails to do so, the county may undertake such restoration at the expense of the selected applicant. 
(c)  Relocation. If at any time during the period of the franchise the county shall lawfully select to alter or change the grade or alignment of any street, alley or other public way the selected applicant, upon reasonable notice by the county, shall remove, relay and relocate its equipment at its own expense. 
(d)  Placement of fixtures. The selected applicant shall not place any fixtures or equipment where the same will interfere with any existing gas, electric, telephone or sewer and water lines, fixtures and equipment, and the locations by the selected applicant of its lines and equipment shall be in such a manner as to not interfere with the usual travel on the streets, alleys and public ways and the use of the same by gas, electric, telephone and water and sewer lines and equipment. 
(e)  Temporary removal of wires for building moving. The selected applicant shall on the request of the county temporarily raise or lower its wires to permit the moving of buildings, but may reserve the right to recover its costs from the person or persons having the building. 
(f)  No property right. Nothing in the franchise shall grant to the selected applicant any right of property in the county-owned property, nor shall the county be compelled to maintain any of its property any longer than, or in any fashion other than, in the county's judgment, its own business or needs may require. 
(g)  Nonliability of county. The county shall not be liable for any damage occurring to the property of the selected applicant caused by employees of the county in the performance of their duties, nor shall the county be held liable for the interruption of service by actions of county employees in the performance of their duties, nor shall the county be held for the failure of the selected applicant to be able to perform normal service due to acts of God. 
(h)  Permits, easements and agreements. The county shall not be required to assume any responsibility for the securing of any permits or agreements with other persons or utilities. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(III)) 
Cross reference— Roads and highways, Ch. 12. 
Sec. 7-60. - Construction approval by county; correction of defects. 
Except for additional connections for ten (10) residences or less, unless the same involves the cutting of a road, the selected applicant shall not erect any pole, run any line, make any attachment nor shall any construction of any kind be commenced without the prior approval of the board of commissioners. The approval as referenced herein shall be in the form of a permit issued by the board upon approval of: 
(1)  Layout maps of the system authorized by the franchise showing plant routing, utility company poles to which the system facilities are to be attached and location of all trunk and distribution line amplifiers; or 
(2)  A certification by applicant that all attachment requests and subsequent approvals required have been obtained. 
The county shall have and maintain the right to inspect the construction, operation and maintenance of the system by the selected applicant to ensure the proper performance of the terms of the franchise. If the selected applicant should violate any of the terms of this article or any of the rules and regulations as may from time to time be lawfully adopted, the county shall immediately give the selected applicant thirty (30) days' written notice to correct such violation. If the selected applicant does not make the correction within thirty (30) days from the receipt of such written notice, the county may make such correction itself and charge the cost of same to the selected applicant. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(IV)) 
Sec. 7-61. - Number of channels. 
(a)  The selected applicant shall maintain and relay to the subscribers to the system in the county not less than the number of channels provided to subscribers in the city from which the applicant originates transmission. 
(b)  Carriage of television signals shall be consistent with those allowed by FCC rules. In addition to television signals allowed by the FCC signal carriage rules, the system shall provide one (1) twenty-four-hour local service channel with local weather information and public service messages. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(V)) 
Sec. 7-62. - Prohibition from engaging in radio and television sales, service and repair. 
The selected applicant and any and all of its officers, agents and employees are specifically prohibited from engaging in the sale, service, rental or leasing of television receivers, radio receivers or television or radio receiver related parts and accessories with any person anywhere in the county, whether for a fee or charge, except for such special devices as may be necessary for the subscriber to receive the requested service. The selected applicant shall prohibit any of its officers, agents and employees from violating the terms of this section at all times, whether in the performance of the duties of the selected applicant or otherwise. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(VI)) 
Sec. 7-63. - Public service, education service. 
(a)  Public service. The selected applicant shall provide, without charge, one (1) outlet to each public office building, recreation department building, fire station, police station and public and private school that is passed by its cable. If more than one (1) outlet is required at any of the locations, the selected applicant shall install at the cost of time and material only and in no event will there be a monthly service charge at the location. 
(b)  Educational service. The selected applicant shall reserve at least one (1) television channel for the use of educational institutions within the county for the origination of educational television telecasts and the interconnection of all of such educational institutions. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(VII)) 
Sec. 7-64. - Service standards. 
(a)  The selected applicant shall maintain and operate the system and render efficient service in accordance with the rules and regulations as now or hereafter may be established by the Federal Communications Commission or its successor. 
(b)  The selected applicant shall be responsible for installation and maintenance of the service wiring from the cable point of entrance to the TV set. 
(c)  The selected applicant shall investigate and resolve all subscriber complaints regarding the quality of service, equipment, malfunctions and similar matters expeditiously and in accordance with the following procedure: 
(1)  The selected applicant shall during normal working hours have qualified personnel available to investigate and resolve subscriber complaints. 
(2)  Upon notification of a service complaint, the selected applicant shall dispatch a qualified employee to investigate the complaint and adjust, repair or replace equipment as necessary to resolve the complaint. The selected applicant shall not be responsible for malfunctions in any subscriber's radio or television receiver. 
(3)  Complaints shall be investigated and resolved within twenty-four (24) hours of notification. If upon investigation it is determined that the complaint cannot be resolved within twenty-four (24) hours due to circumstances beyond the control of the selected applicant, the subscriber shall be notified and given an estimation as to when the complaint will be resolved. 
(d)  The selected applicant shall be required to provide permanent service to any permanent-type residence within a period of ninety (90) working days from the initial request for service from potential subscribers when the area requesting service has an average of thirty (30) residences per contiguous mile with existing service. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(VIII)) 
Sec. 7-65. - Company rules. 
(a)  The selected applicant shall have the authority to promulgate such rules, regulations, terms and conditions governing the conduct of its business as shall be reasonably necessary to enable the selected applicant to exercise its rights and to perform its obligations under the franchise and to assure an uninterrupted service to each and all its subscribers; provided, however, that such rules, regulations, terms and conditions shall not be in conflict with the provisions of this article and shall be filed with the county and shall be subject to the approval of the county. 
(b)  The selected applicant shall not refuse to hire or employ, nor bar or discharge from employment, nor discriminate against any person in compensation or in terms, conditions or privileges of employment because of sex, race, creed, color, marital status or national origin. This requirement shall apply to, but not be limited to, the following: employment, upgrading, demotion or transfer, recruitment advertising, layoff or termination, rates of pay or other forms of compensation and selection of training. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(IX)) 
Sec. 7-66. - Local office. 
The selected applicant shall throughout the duration of any franchise maintain an office open to the public during reasonable business hours and a system manager for performing services and meeting all requirements provided herein. The office shall be located within the county or within a fifteen-mile radius of the county line; if the office is located beyond the certified telephone area in which the system operates, a toll-free line shall be provided for subscribers. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(X)) 
Sec. 7-67. - County rules, control of rates and payments. 
The right is hereby reserved to the county to adopt, in addition to the provisions contained in this article and in existing applicable resolutions or ordinances, such additional regulations as the county may find necessary in the exercise of police power, provided such regulations by resolution or ordinance otherwise shall be reasonable and not in conflict with the rights herein granted. Except as otherwise herein limited, the county shall approve the rates and costs to the subscribers of the system in the county and the county shall have the right to set the amount of payments required of the selected applicant to the county. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XI)) 
Sec. 7-68. - Occupational licenses, taxes, etc. 
The selected applicant shall pay annually, in addition to the franchise fee, such ad valorem and personal property taxes, inventory taxes, occupational licenses, fees and service charges as shall be appropriate to that general classification of business as set forth by law. It is herewith noted the selected applicant is not classified as a public utility and therefore not subject to payment of any type of utility taxes. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XII)) 
Cross reference— Taxation, Ch. 16. 
Sec. 7-69. - Rates to subscribers. 
The selected applicant may make such charges for its services as are reasonable. The selected applicant may increase these rates annually but no more than ten (10) percent per year, which percentage is cumulative up to, but not to exceed, thirty (30) percent without prior approval of the county. The applicant's subscribers located in the unincorporated areas of the county shall not be charged a greater rate than the applicants' subscribers located in the incorporated area from which the system originates for the same or equivalent service. A subscriber of the selected applicant may discontinue any service provided by the applicant at any time without further charge or penalty. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XIII)) 
Sec. 7-70. - Payments to county. 
(a)  Gross subscriber revenue tax. The selected applicant shall pay to the county the standard or franchise fee based on gross subscriber revenues received from its operations in the county in an amount not to exceed that amount authorized under applicable federal law and regulations. 
(b)  Manner of payment. All payments as required by the selected applicant to the county shall be made quarterly and shall be due within fifteen (15) days from first day of each calendar quarter unless the same shall fall on a weekend or legal holiday, in which event the same shall be paid on the next immediate work day. A late penalty of ten (10) percent shall be assessed on any payment made more than fifteen (15) days after the due date. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XIV)) 
Sec. 7-71. - Records and reports. 
The county shall have access at all reasonable hours to the selected applicant's records relating to subscriber revenue, which are deemed necessary by the county to determine compliance with this article and the contract between the selected applicant and the county. An annual summary report showing gross subscriber revenues received by the selected applicant from the operation of the system within the county during the preceding twelve-month period and such other information as the county may require in support of same shall be given to the county by the selected applicant. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XV)) 
Sec. 7-72. - Transfer approval. 
The selected applicant shall not sell or transfer its plant or system or any portion thereof, nor any right, title or interest in the same, nor shall the selected applicant transfer any rights under the franchise to any other person without prior approval of the board of commissioners, which approval shall not be unreasonably or arbitrarily withheld. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XVI)) 
Sec. 7-73. - Duration of franchise. 
Any franchise granted pursuant to this article shall be for such period of time as may be agreed upon between the selected applicant and the county and shall be subject to renewal by the county by negotiations upon reasonable terms with the selected applicant for an additional period. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XVII)) 
Sec. 7-74. - Penalties. 
(a)  Should the selected applicant, its successors or assigns violate any of the provisions of the franchise, any ordinance or any reasonable rules and regulations or other laws or should the selected applicant fail to promptly perform any of the provisions hereof, the selected applicant shall forfeit all its rights hereunder to the county after written notice and hearing before the board of commissioners or its duly appointed hearing officer to the selected applicant. The continuation of such violation, failure or default for a period of more than thirty (30) days after the hearing shall constitute default of the contract and loss of all rights and privileges thereunder. Failure to perform any of the provisions of the franchise shall constitute default on the part of the selected applicant, and upon default the selected applicant shall forfeit all of its rights and privileges under the franchise and at the option of the county have the agreement terminated without further notice, provided that acts of God or events or happenings beyond the control of the selected applicant shall not be grounds for termination. 
(b)  In the event of the bankruptcy or receivership for the selected applicant, all rights herein given to the selected applicant shall, at the option of the county, be forfeited and terminated. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XVIII)) 
Sec. 7-75. - Termination of negotiations. 
At any time the board of commissioners may terminate negotiations and begin negotiations with any other selected applicant or may select other applicants for negotiation. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XIX)) 
Sec. 7-76. - Granting of franchise. 
(a)  After negotiations with the selected applicant are completed and the selected applicant has met all requirements of the county, the board of commissioners may by contract, which shall include all terms and conditions negotiated by the county and the selected applicant, grant a CATV franchise to the selected applicant, which shall be nonexclusive. 
(b)  The county may issue as many CATV franchises as it deems appropriate without regard to any service area of any other CATV franchise. 
(Ord. of 11-21-89, § 6(XX)) 
Secs. 7-77—7-100. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - MALT BEVERAGE, WINE AND LIQUOR ORDINANCE[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
Editor's note— An ordinance adopted July 10, 2012, §§ 1(I—XXV), amended Art. IV in its entirety to read as set out herein. Former Art. IV, §§ 7-101—7-115, pertained to malt beverage and wine licenses and derived from Ord. of 10-15-91, §§ I—XV; Mo. of 1-17-95; Ord. of 7-1-97, §§ 1, 2; Ord. of 1-16-01; Ord. of 8-19-03, § 1; Ord. of 1-2-07, §§ A—D; Ord. of 5-20-08, §§ 1, 2. 
Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, Ch. 3. 

Sec. 7-101. - Short title, purpose and privilege. 
This article shall be known and may be cited as the "Malt Beverage, Wine and Liquor Ordinance of Gordon County." The purpose of this article is to provide procedures, rules and regulations governing the issuance of licenses for the retail sale of alcoholic beverages and for consumption on the premises of alcoholic beverages in the appropriate establishments as allowed by this article. 
Any license which is issued allowing for the sale of alcoholic beverages in the unincorporated area of Gordon County may be issued by the commission pursuant to the rules and regulations set forth in this article. The holding of any such license or licensees is declared to be a privilege and not a right. 
(Ord. of 7-10-12, § I) 
Sec. 7-102. - Definitions. 
For the purpose of this article, the following terms, phrases, words and their derivations shall have the meaning given herein. When not inconsistent with the context, words used in the present tense include the future, words in the plural number include the singular number, and words in the singular include the plural number. 
Alcoholic beverage means and includes all alcohol, distilled spirits, malt beverages, wine or fortified wine. 
Alcoholic beverage caterer means any person that has obtained an off-premises catering license to sell and/or distribute alcoholic beverages by the drink. 
Authorized catered function means an event for which an event permit has been issued pursuant to section 7-109 of this article for the sale and/or distribution of alcoholic beverages by the drink for consumption at such event. 
Bona fide nonprofit civic organization means an entity which is exempt from Federal Income Tax pursuant to the provisions of subsection c. of 26 U.S.C. Section 501. 
Building means any structure having a roof supported by columns or walls intended for shelter, housing or enclosure of persons. 
Commission means the Board of Commissioners of Gordon County. 
Consumption on the premises means the sale or offering to sell alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wine for consumption on the premises at retail only to consumers and not for resale. The license issued to such person shall be known as a "Consumption on the Premises License." 
Department means the Department of Revenue of the State of Georgia. 
Distilled spirits means all beverages, containing any alcohol obtained by distillation or containing more than twenty-one (21) percent alcohol by volume including, but not limited to, all fortified wines. 
Gallon or wine gallon means a United States gallon of liquid measure equivalent to the volume of two hundred thirty-one (231) cubic inches or the nearest equivalent metric measurement. 
Individual means a natural person. 
Keg means a barrel or bulk container of malt beverage commonly known as tap or draft beer. 
License officer is the Gordon County Clerk or designee. 
Licensed premises means the building and/or real property described in the license application as approved by the county commission where the sale of alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wines is permitted to be sold. 
Licensed retailer means any person (not a producer) selling or offering to sell alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wine in an original package not for consumption on the premises where sold and holding a valid license issued by Gordon County and the State of Georgia. 
Licensed wholesaler means any person (not a producer) who sells or offers to sell alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wine for purposes of resale to licensed retailers, to licensed wholesalers, or to persons holding a consumption on the premises license. 
Malt beverages means any alcoholic beverages obtained by fermentation of any infusion or decoction of barley, malt, hops, or any similar product, or any combination of such product in water, containing not more than six (6) percent alcohol by volume. 
Package means a bottle, can, keg, barrel or other original consumer container, as delivered by a licensed wholesaler to a licensed retailer. 
Package store means a store licensed by Gordon County and the State of Georgia to sell distilled spirits not for consumption on the premises. 
Person means an individual, firm, partnership, corporation, association, company, agency, syndicate, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, fiduciary or any combination acting as a unit, body politic, or political subdivision whether public, private or quasi-public. 
Retail consumption dealer means any person who sells or offers to sell alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wine for consumption on the licensed premises. 
Taxpayer means any person made liable by law to file a return or to pay tax. 
Wine means all alcoholic beverages containing not more than twenty-one (21) percent alcohol by volume made from fruit, berries, or grapes, either by natural fermentation or by natural fermentation with brandy added. "Wine" includes, but is not limited to, all sparkling wines, champagnes, combinations of such beverages, vermouths, special natural wines, rectified wines and like products. The term does not include cooking wine mixed with salt or other ingredients so as to render it unfit for human consumption as a beverage. 
(Ord. of 7-10-12, § II) 
Sec. 7-103. - In certain retail establishments only—For consumption on premises. 
Alcoholic beverages, wine or malt beverages shall not be sold at retail for consumption on premises except in the following types of businesses: 
(1)  In restaurants, other than fast food restaurants, serving prepared food which is offered to the general public and where chairs, tables and counters are provided to seat and service twenty-five (25) or more persons. Such establishments shall be located in zoning districts that permit restaurants and shall meet the criteria set out in this article concerning the hours of sale. 
For the purpose of this article, a fast food restaurant is defined as a restaurant that derives more than fifteen (15) percent of its sales by use of a carry-out window serving persons outside the building, who are either on foot or who are the occupants of motor vehicles. 
(2)  In hotels or motels, kept, used, maintained, advertised and held out to the general public to be a place where food is served and consumed, and sleeping accommodations are offered for adequate rates to travelers and guests, whether transient, permanent or residential, in which forty (40) or more rooms are used for sleeping accommodations for guests. 
(3)  In lounges where seating accommodations are provided for not less than twenty-five (25) persons, where such establishments are located in zoning districts where such establishments are permitted or in a district where existing lounges exist as a nonconforming use. In addition, the lounge shall meet the criteria set out in this article concerning the application process. 
(4)  In private clubs authorized and existing under the laws of the State of Georgia, or a bona fide association of individuals organized for fraternal purposes, conducted solely for the benefit of its members and their beneficiaries, operated on the lodge system with ritualistic form of work, having a representative form of government and at least seventy-five (75) members paying monthly dues, where no part of the net earnings of which shall inure to the benefit of any shareholder or member, provided further that no member, officer or agent, or employee of the club is compensated, directly or indirectly, by any form of commission or other compensation based on the amount of profit from the sale of alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wine beyond the amount of such salary as may be fixed by its members or by its governing body out of the general revenue of the club. For the purpose of this subsection, tips which are added to the bills under club regulations shall not be considered as profits hereunder. 
(5)  In bowling alleys, provided that the following rules and regulations are followed: 
a.  No alcoholic beverages will be consumed on or upon the bowling lanes or the approach area of such lanes, but only in a seating area set aside for spectators located separately and apart from the bowling lanes; 
b.  No alcoholic beverages will be served in any part of the bowling alley prior to 12:00 noon on Monday through Saturday; and 
c.  No alcoholic beverages will be sold on Sundays. 
(6)  Alcoholic beverages, malt beverages and wine for consumption on premises, in addition to the places set out in subparagraphs (1) through (5) of this section, may also be sold in refreshment stands or clubhouses located within the boundaries of golf courses or race tracks. 
(Ord. of 7-10-12, § III) 
Sec. 7-104. - Unlawful practices. 
It shall be unlawful for any adult entertainment establishment licensee, as defined in the Gordon County Adult Entertainment Ordinance and issued pursuant to that article, to serve, sell, distribute or suffer the consumption or possession of alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wine upon the premises of that said licensee. In addition, it shall be unlawful for any licensee holding a license for the sale of alcoholic beverages of any kind to permit, perform, promote, advertise, stage, suffer, or in any way to allow any person to expose specified anatomical areas or engage in specified sexual activities in, on or about the licensed premises. 
Definitions. As used in this section, these terms shall have the following meanings: 
(1)  Specified anatomical areas shall include any of the following: 
a.  Less than completely and opaquely covered human genitals or pubic region; buttock; or female breast below a point immediately above the top of the areola; or 
b.  Human male genitalia in a discernible turgid state, even if completely and opaquely covered. 
(2)  Specified sexual activities means and shall include any of the following: 
a.  Actual or simulated sexual intercourse, oral copulation, anal intercourse, oral and anal copulation, bestiality, direct physical stimulation of unclothed genitals, flagellation or torture in the context of a sexual relationship, or the use of excretory functions in the context of a sexual relationship and any of the following sexually oriented acts or conduct: anilingus, buggery, coprophagy, cunnilingus, fellatio, necrophilia, pederasty, pedophilia, piquerism, sapphism, zooerasty; or 
b.  Clearly depicted human genitals in a state of sexual stimulation, arousal or tumescence; or 
c.  Use of human or animal ejaculation, sodomy, or oral copulation, coitus or masturbation; or 
d.  Fondling or touching of nude human genitals, pubic region, buttocks, or female breast; or 
e.  Masochism, erotic or sexually oriented torture, beating or the infliction of pain; or 
f.  Erotic lewd touching, fondling or other sexual contact with an animal by a human being; or 
g.  Human excretion, urination, menstruation, vaginal or anal irrigation. 
(Ord. of 7-10-12, § IV) 
Sec. 7-105. - Sale of malt beverages and wine—Not for consumption on premises. 
No malt beverages or wines shall be sold at retail except as follows: 
(1)  In retail stores devoted principally to the sale of groceries and food products to the general public and located in zoning districts in which food or convenience stores are permitted as a conforming use or in districts where existing food or convenience stores exist as a nonconforming use. In order for a store to be devoted principally to the sale of groceries and food products, the building must contain at least one thousand (1,000) square feet and seventy (70) percent of the retail floor area of the building must be devoted exclusively to the sale of groceries or related grocery items. For the purpose of this article, groceries and related grocery items are defined so as to exclude any drinks containing any amount of alcohol. 
(2)  In a facility duly licensed by Gordon County to sell at retail malt beverages or wines in the original unbroken package. 
(3)  No malt beverages or wines shall be displayed for sale or sold on the licensed premises, other than in an air-cooled cooler which is operated by means of electrical current, except that this section shall not apply to malt beverages or wines which are stored and displayed at room temperature in the original package. 
(4)  All licensees selling kegs of malt beverages shall, at the time of the such sale, record the serial number of the keg along with the name and address of the buyer. Further, the licensee shall require the buyer to provide documentation, in the form of a driver's license, etc., to verify the identity of the buyer. Said record shall be maintained for a period of six (6) months, and shall be provided to the Gordon County Sheriff's Department upon request. For the purposes of this subsection, the form utilized the Georgia Department of Revenue, Alcohol and Tobacco Division, properly filled out, shall be sufficient to satisfy the information retention requirements herein. 
(Ord. of 7-10-12, § V) 
Sec. 7-106. - Hotel in-room service license. 
Any hotel, motel, inn or other establishments which meet the requirements set out in subsection 7-103(2) is hereby authorized to provide in-room service as defined in this section. In order to qualify for a hotel-in-room service, the applicant must satisfy the following requirements: 
(1)  Applicant must be the current holder of a retail dealer license, a retail consumption deal license, a retail beer dealer license or a retail wine dealer license; provided, however the applicant may only qualify for a hotel-in-room service license for the type of alcoholic beverage for which he holds a current license. 
(2)  Applicant shall apply on a form provided by Gordon County specifying the type of in-room service license sought (beer, wine, distilled spirits or any combination thereof) together with any other forms, documentation, or other information required by the Gordon County Board of Commissioners. 
(3)  A hotel in-room service licensee shall be authorized to deliver alcoholic beverages, either by the package or by the drink, if the hotel holds a valid in-room service license, by a hotel employee to a registered guest's room when such distilled spirits, malt beverages or wine have been ordered by the guest and when the guest shall be billed for the cost of such alcoholic beverages, at the time of the delivery; provided further, however, such sale shall be evidenced by a signed receipt indicating which guest ordered alcoholic beverages, indicating the identification and quantity of alcoholic beverages, malt beverages and wine actually delivered; provided, however, that the hotel may provide the guest with a credit for any unused and unopened alcoholic beverages. 
(4)  All hotels having in-room service shall comply with all requirements promulgated by the Department of Revenue of the State of Georgia dealing with storage of alcoholic beverages and records required to be maintained in order to provide hotel in-room service. 
(5)  Nothing contained in this article shall be construed to restrict or prohibit possession of alcoholic beverages by hotel guests in quantities otherwise permitted by O.C.G.A. tit. 3. 
(Ord. of 7-10-12, § VI) 
Sec. 7-107. - Regulations for operation of business. 
(a)  Hours of operation. The following hours of sale are hereby established for the alcoholic beverages, malt beverages or wine: 
(1)  No sale of alcoholic beverages by the package and/or wine shall be allowed except between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 11:00 p.m. on weekdays and on Saturdays. 
(2)  No sale of alcoholic beverages for consumption on the premises shall be allowed except between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 12:00 a.m. (midnight) on weekdays and on Saturdays.
