ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 10-1. - County personnel system. 
The Gordon County Personnel Policies create a system of employment which recognizes that the county employees covered by the system should be selected and promoted according to their skills, knowledge and abilities, and that employees who perform satisfactorily should be retained in their positions as long as the positions exist and regardless of factors not associated with their performance and conduct compatible with the trust inherent in public service, the administrative necessity for the position held, availability of funds and organizational needs of the government unit. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 1, § A) 
Sec. 10-2. - Establishment. 
These policies have been established by the Gordon County Board of Commissioners, hereinafter referred to as the "board." The board and participating elected officials have included specified employees under their administration in the system. This action was taken to provide a fair, equitable, and productive work environment. The system and these policies have been enabled by the signatures of the participating elected officials and by an ordinance adopted by the board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 1, § B) 
Sec. 10-3. - Purpose. 
These policies have been adopted to provide for the recruitment and development of the best available employee for each position in the service of the county. They provide for the establishment of orderly procedures for administering the following principles: 
(1)  Recruiting, selecting and advancing employees on the basis of their relative ability, knowledge and skills, including open competition of qualified applicants for initial appointment. 
(2)  Establishing pay rates consistent with the principle of providing comparable pay for comparable work. 
(3)  Training employees, as needed, to assure high-quality performance. 
(4)  Retraining employees on the basis of the adequacy of their performance, correcting inadequate performance, and separating employees from the work force whose inadequate performance cannot be corrected. 
(5)  Assuring equal employment opportunity through the fair treatment of applicants and employees in all aspects of personnel administration without regard to political affiliation, race, color, creed, national origin or ancestry, disability, sex, or religion and with proper regard for their privacy and constitutional rights as citizens. 
(6)  Assuring that employees are protected against coercion for partisan political purposes and are prohibited from using their official authority for the purpose of interfering with or affecting the results of an election or a nomination for office. 
(7)  Establishing uniform benefits and personnel procedures where applicable. 
(8)  Complying with applicable federal and state laws. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 1, § C) 
State Law reference— Employment of blind, visually handicapped, deaf and otherwise physically disabled persons, O.C.G.A. §§ 30-1-2, 34-6A-1 et seq.; age discrimination in employment, O.C.G.A. § 34-1-2; discrimination against employee for attending judicial proceeding in response to court order or process, O.C.G.A. § 34-1-3; sex discrimination in employment, O.C.G.A. § 34-5-1 et seq. 
Sec. 10-4. - Positions covered. 
These policies apply to the career service positions in all departments under the administration of the board and of the participating elected officials, including those employees whose positions are subsidized from federal, state or other sources. The following are the exceptions: 
(1)  Federal equal employment law recognizes that neither elected officials nor members of their personal staffs should be covered by legislation creating full-time positions, and O.C.G.A. § 36-1-21 exempts elected officials or persons appointed to positions for specified terms from civil service coverage. Therefore, the board and the participating elected officials will determine which positions in the county are policy-making, personal staff, or appointments for specified terms, and shall exclude these positions from coverage under these policies. All other full-time and part-time positions that are included in the classification plan are covered. 
(2)  Employees of other agencies partially funded by the county and employees of departments jointly funded by the county and municipalities and/or organizations located within the geographic boundaries of the county. 
(3)  Members of appointed or elected boards, commissions or authorities. 
(4)  Employees who have been employed by the county for less than six (6) months or who are on an extended initial working test period. 
(5)  Part-time or temporary positions unless specifically covered by action of the board. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 1, § D) 
Sec. 10-5. - Administration and enforcement. 
The county administrator, as the chief executive officer of the county, with the cooperation of the participating elected officials, is responsible for administering and maintaining these policies. The daily implementation and routine administrative duties associated with the system and the policies may be delegated to the human resources director. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 1, § E) 
Cross reference— Administration, Ch. 2. 
Sec. 10-6. - Policy changes. 
The board reserves the right to change or amend these policies at any time, by resolution, if the change does not adversely affect the property interests of the employees. Proposed changes will be provided to participating elected officials for their review, comment, and approval. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 1, § F) 
Sec. 10-7. - Definitions. 
For the purpose of explaining and clarifying the personnel policies of the county, the following words and phrases shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section of word definitions. 
Anniversary date is the date one (1) year from the initial employment date. For leave purposes, the anniversary date shall be that date each subsequent year from the initial date of employment. 
Appeal means the right to appear before the county administrator, or his designee, or the appropriate authority so designated by this chapter to be heard on matters of discrimination, unfair practices, or other rights of applicants or employees under these policies and for review of decisions by the county. 
Board of commissioners or board means the legislative body of the county. 
Career service includes all jobs subject to the terms of the personnel policies, except for those specifically exempted. 
Class means a group of positions sufficiently similar as to the duties performed, degree of supervision exercised or required, minimum requirements of training, experience, and such other characteristics, that the same title, the same tests of fitness, the same schedule of compensation may be applied to each position in the group; and which has been recognized as such in the classification plan established and approved by the county. 
Continuous service is employment which is uninterrupted except for authorized leaves of absence, suspension, or separation due to a reduction in the work force. 
Demotion means the reduction of a regular or working test employee to a position of a lower class. For this purpose, a lower class means a class having a minimum salary lower than the maximum salary for the position in which the individual is employed. 
Department head means any county employee designated as the head or principal administrative officer of any department established in the internal organization of the county as an administrative medium of the county administrator and subordinate to the county administrator. For the purposes of this chapter, the term "department head" may also refer to an elected official or a judicial official. 
Employee means an incumbent of a position as hereinafter defined. 
Exempt employee means an employee who is exempt from the provisions of the wage and hour laws of the Fair Labor Standards Act. All department heads are considered to be exempt employees. 
Full-time position means any employee in a regular position who is scheduled to work at least thirty (30) hours per week. 
Merit increase means a pay adjustment earned due to length of service and satisfactory performance as determined by existing policies and available funding. 
Nonexempt employee means an employee who is covered by the provisions of the wage and hour laws of the Fair Labor Standards Act. 
Open competitive vacancy means a position wherein announcement of a vacancy and acceptance of applications is solicited from every segment of the community. 
Part time means any employee working less than thirty (30) hours per week on a continuing basis. 
Performance evaluation means a method of evaluating each employee on a periodic basis as to his performance on the job. 
Position means a job, whether part-time or full-time, temporary or regular, occupied or vacant, composed of specific duties and responsibilities requiring the services of one (1) person. 
Promotion means the filling of a vacancy by the advancement of a regular employee from a position of a lower class. For this purpose, a lower class means any class of positions having a maximum salary lower than the maximum salary of the vacant position. 
Promotional competitive vacancy means a position wherein announcement of a vacancy and acceptance of applications is confined to employees of the county. 
Public notice, unless otherwise expressly stated, means a written notice on a bulletin board accessible to the public during business hours, and other publicity as may be deemed necessary by the county administrator or his designee. 
Regular employee is an employee who has completed his working test period in a satisfactory manner and has obtained status in the career service. 
Resignation means an action separating an employee at his own written or verbal request and is accepted without prejudice, provided that the resignation is not offered to avoid removal for cause. If a resignation is offered to avoid removal for cause, it will not be accepted as a resignation unless it is determined to be clearly in the best interest of the county. A resignation is effective immediately upon acceptance and no further administrative action is required to validate that resignation. 
Salary advancement means an increase in salary, based on quality and length of service within the salary range prescribed for a particular class of positions. 
Salary range adjustment means the allocation of a classification to a higher or lower salary range, due to legislative or administrative action. 
Status is acquired by the satisfactory completion of a working test period by an employee in the classified service. 
Suspension means the temporary removal of an employee from the county for either disciplinary purposes or pending investigation of charges against the employee. A suspension may be with or without pay. 
Temporary employees means those engaged for special activities of the county for a specific period with the definite understanding that their employment is to terminate at the end of the period. Temporary employees will be considered either full-time or part-time, depending upon the number of hours worked per week. No temporary employee will be eligible to accrue privileges or benefits under the provisions of the fringe benefits, insurance and retirement plans. 
Transfer means an action to change an employee from a position in one (1) department to a position in another department within the same classification or a change from one (1) class to another class in the same pay grade. Where an increase or decrease of pay grade is involved, the action will be designated as a "promotion" or a "demotion." 
Vacancy is a position duly created and still existent but not occupied by an employee. 
Working test period describes the status of a newly appointed or promoted employee who is required to serve a six-month working test period to demonstrate satisfactory job performance and who may be released from employment or returned to pre-promotion status without recourse. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 1, § G) 
Editor's note— General rules of construction; definitions, § 1-2. 
Sec. 10-8. - Effective date. 
These policies shall become effective on the date adopted, by resolution of the county, and shall remain in effect until duly amended. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XIX, § A) 
Sec. 10-9. - Amendment of personnel policies. 
These policies may be amended from time to time by a majority vote of the county board of commissioners. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XIX, § D) 
Secs. 10-10—10-25. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PERSONNEL SYSTEM 

Sec. 10-26. - Applications and examinations. 
(a)  Announcement of vacant positions. Vacancies shall be publicized by posting announcements at the county courthouse or in other places, and by such other means as the county administrator and the human resources director deem advisable for positions for which the county administrator is the hiring authority. Elected officials may establish their own policies for recruitment and selection of vacant positions. Receipt of applications may be limited to present employees or may be opened to the public. The announcements shall: 
(1)  Specify the title and salary range of the vacant positions, qualification requirements, manner of making application, and other pertinent information. 
(2)  Specify the form of the examination if required for the positions. 
(b)  Application forms. Application shall be made on forms provided by the human resources director. Such forms shall require information covering training, experience, and other pertinent information. All applications shall be signed by the applicant. 
(c)  Employment requirements. All positions shall be open to persons who meet the requirements as listed on the public announcement of the examination. Such requirements may include, but shall not be limited to, the following factors: 
(1)  Experience. 
(2)  Education. 
(3)  Training. 
(d)  Receipt and duration of applications. Applications will be accepted only when there is an advertised opening for a position. The applications will be placed on file from all persons desiring employment with the county, and who apply during regular business hours. In order to be considered for employment, all applicants for employment must complete an employment application. All persons shall be informed at the time of application that applications will be placed in an active file for a period of forty-five (45) days. Should another position become available during the forty-five-day period for which a rejected applicant wishes to be considered, the rejected applicant should contact the human resources director and request consideration. 
(e)  Rejection of applications. The human resources director may reject an application which indicates that the applicant is deficient in any or all of the requirements as specified in the public announcement of the vacancy. An application may also be rejected for the practice, or attempted practice, of fraud or deception in the completion of his application or if his past record of employment is determined by the human resources director to be unsatisfactory. Notice of rejection, stating the reason therefor, shall be mailed to the rejected applicant by the human resources director. 
(f)  Open competitive appointments. Positions to be filled by recruitment, from outside the career service, shall be filled through a competitive process open to the public. Such process may include, but not be limited to, ratings of training and experience, written, oral, physical, or performance tests, or any combination of these as determined by the human resources director. The process may take into consideration such factors as education, experience, knowledge, skill, physical fitness, or any other bona fide occupational qualifications which are job-related and which, in the judgment of the human resources director, enter into the determination of the relative suitability of applicants. The human resources director may require the applicant to submit proof of his education, military service, or any other such documentation as he/she deems necessary. All qualifications and tests shall be job-related and shall be administered in a nondiscriminatory manner. 
(g)  Promotional appointments. Promotional appointments shall be open to all employees, who meet the training and experience requirements included in the class specification, or who have an equivalent combination of experience and training which provides the required knowledge, skills, and abilities. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 2) 
Sec. 10-27. - Appointments. 
(a)  Types of appointments. When a person is initially employed by the county, they shall be given one (1) of the following types of original appointments: 
(1)  Working test. An appointment to a position in the career service. 
(2)  Provisional. An appointment made only in the absence of a qualified applicant. 
a.  When there is a need to fill a vacancy, and a qualified applicant is not available, a provisional appointment may be made. 
b.  Provisional appointments shall not exceed six (6) months. However, extensions may be approved by the county administrator, elected official, or judicial official, where applicable. 
c.  An employee shall not attain regular status while serving on a provisional appointment. 
(3)  Temporary. Temporary appointments may be made to fill positions when the work of the county requires the services of one (1) or more employees on a seasonal or intermittent basis, or in cases of emergency. Temporary appointments shall not exceed one (1) year's consecutive duration. 
(b)  Regular appointment. A career employee, given an original working test appointment, shall be given a regular appointment upon satisfactory completion of the working test period and shall acquire regular status. A working test promotional appointment does not affect an employee's earned regular status and rights acquired in another position. 
(c)  Hiring authority. The county administrator shall serve as the hiring authority for all positions, except for those positions in the department of the elected officials and the judicial officials. The elected officials and the judicial officials shall serve as the hiring authority in their respective departments. Prior to extending an offer of employment to any person as a department head, the county administrator shall make a recommendation to and receive approval from the board of commissioners for that offer of employment as a department head. The board of commissioners, based upon the recommendation of the county administrator, shall approve said offer of employment as a department head by a majority vote, with at least three (3) commission members affirming the recommendation of the county administrator. In addition, prior to advertising any newly created position for county employment, the county administrator shall likewise obtain approval by a majority vote of the board of commissioners, with at least three (3) commission members voting in the affirmative, for the advertisement of the newly created position. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 3; Ord. of 9-2-03, § 1) 
Sec. 10-28. - Working test period. 
(a)  Objective. The working test period shall be regarded as an integral part of the selection process and shall be utilized for closely observing the employee's work, for securing the most effective adjustment of a new employee to his position, and for rejecting any employee whose performance is not satisfactory. 
(b)  Duration. The working test period shall be six (6) months in duration. 
(c)  Promotional appointments. The working test period shall be used in connection with promotional appointments in the same manner as it is used for original entrance appointments. If a person is removed during his working test period following a promotion, he may be considered for return to his former position, or a similar position, if one is available. 
(d)  Interruption of working test. If an employee is laid off during a working test period, and his services have been satisfactory and he is subsequently reemployed in the same department, he shall be given credit for the portion of the working test period completed before he was laid off. 
(e)  Dismissal during working test. During the working test period, an employee may be terminated for the following reasons: 
(1)  At any time during the working test period, the department head may remove an employee if, in the department head's opinion, the working test period indicates that such employee is unable or unwilling to perform the duties of the position satisfactorily, or that his habits and the lack of dependability do not merit his continuance with the service, or for causes which would subject a regular employee to disciplinary action. A report in writing shall be sent to the human resources director within three (3) days after the effective date of the dismissal. 
(2)  An employee found to have been appointed through fraud shall be removed within ten (10) calendar days of notification of the department head to this effect. 
(3)  A department head may demote an employee to a lower class position during the working test period. A written report of such demotion and the reasons therefor must be filed with the human resources director within three (3) days after the effective date of the demotion. 
(4)  Working test period reports. At least twenty (20) working days prior to the expiration of the employee's working test period, the department head shall notify the human resources director, in writing, whether the employee has satisfactorily completed, or is expected to satisfactorily complete, his working test period. 
(5)  An employee may be released during the working test period without recourse and as such has no right to avail himself or herself to a grievance procedure. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. 4) 
Sec. 10-29. - Promotions, transfers and demotions. 
(a)  Policy. Vacancies in higher positions in the career service shall be filled, as far as practicable, by promotion from lower classes. To accomplish this purpose, closed examinations may be held. When the county administrator and the human resources director determine that there is a sufficient number of well-qualified eligibles within the service, they may direct that a closed competition be held. 
(b)  Political or partisan endorsement prohibited. No consideration shall be given to political or partisan endorsement for promotions to positions in the classified service; only merit and fitness for promotion shall be considered. 
(c)  Promotional examinations. The human resources director, working in conjunction with appointed department heads, elected officials and/or judicial officials, shall conduct promotional examinations in accordance with these regulations. In promotional examinations, the human resources director shall admit to the process all employees who meet the published qualification requirements. Oral interviews are recognized as one (1) form of promotional examinations. 
(d)  Intradepartmental transfers. The appropriate department head may, at any time, transfer an employee under his jurisdiction from one (1) position to another in the same department upon first obtaining the recommendation of the human resources director and approval of the county administrator. 
(e)  Interdepartmental transfers. A transfer of an employee from one (1) department to another shall have the recommendation of both department heads concerned and the approval of the county administrator or his designee. Requests for such transfer shall show how the employee concerned meets the qualification requirements of the class to which the transfer is proposed. 
(f)  Voluntary demotions. An employee may be voluntarily demoted to a vacant position, in a lower class, subject to approval of his department head and the county administrator. The county administrator shall determine whether the employee is qualified to perform the duties and responsibilities of the lower class of position. No employee shall be voluntarily demoted until he has submitted a written request that such action be considered. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. V) 
Sec. 10-30. - Employee performance evaluation. 
(a)  Objective. The county administrator shall prepare, or cause to be prepared, a job-related system for evaluating the work performance of all employees in the career service. The purpose of the employee performance evaluation shall be primarily to inform employees how well they are performing their work and how they can improve their work performance. The performance evaluation may also be used in determining order of layoff, as a basis for training, promotion, demotion, transfer, or dismissal, and for such other purposes as set forth in these regulations. 
(b)  Period of evaluation. On original appointment, or on promotions, all employees, except temporary workers, shall be evaluated in writing by the supervisor, and a recommendation shall be made within twenty (20) days of the end of their working test period and semiannually thereafter. An employee shall not be eligible for a pay raise until the performance evaluation form has been completely processed. Employees shall also be evaluated at the time of separation. 
(c)  Evaluation. Evaluations shall be prepared by the immediate supervisor of each employee and reviewed by the department head. An employee in a supervisory position, who is leaving the position, may be required to submit performance evaluation forms on all the employees under his supervision who have not been evaluated within the previous six-month period. 
(d)  Review with employees. The evaluator shall discuss each performance evaluation with the employee being evaluated. If an employee disagrees with any statement in an evaluation, he may submit, within ten (10) days following the conference with his supervisor, a written statement which shall be attached to the evaluation form and forwarded to the human resources director. 
(e)  Personnel files and performance evaluations confidential. Personnel files and performance evaluations shall be confidential and shall be made available only to: 
(1)  The employee evaluated. 
(2)  His supervisor or department head. 
(3)  The county administrator or his representative. 
(4)  Attorneys representing the county. 
(f)  Changes in evaluation. If for any reason a department head shall request an alteration of the performance evaluation form, after it has been officially submitted to the human resources director, such request shall be in writing and shall set forth fully the reasons for the request. The employee shall also be notified if a change is made in the evaluation. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. VI) 
Sec. 10-31. - Disciplinary action. 
(a)  Intent. It is the intent of the county that effective supervision and employee relations will avoid most matters which necessitate disciplinary action. These rules, and disciplinary action for violation of such rules, are not intended to restrict the rights of anyone, but to insure the rights of all and to secure cooperation and orderliness throughout the career service. The severity of disciplinary action should be related to the gravity of the offense, the employee's record of disciplinary action, the employee's length of service, and the county's practice in similar cases. 
The department head and the human resources director shall make every effort to insure that all employees understand their duties and are aware of the rules and standards that apply to them. Every effort shall also be made to consistently enforce rules and standards. Fairness, promptness, and legal sufficiency shall govern the disciplinary process. 
In applying these guidelines for disciplinary actions, the concept of "progressive discipline" shall be followed. "Progressive discipline" is defined as meaning that when disciplinary actions are necessary, they are gradually increased and applied in terms of ascending severity. Each action is intended to correct unacceptable behavior. With progressive discipline, employees shall be given an opportunity to correct their behavior before a more severe action is applied. The objective is to apply the least severe action which will improve the employee's performance to an acceptable level. 
(b)  Types of disciplinary action. The forms of discipline to be utilized by the county, when deemed necessary, are as follows: 
(1)  Employee counseling (oral reprimand). When an employee does not comply with the rules and standards of his position, the department head may counsel orally with the employee in order to clearly define areas of deficient job performance and steps needed for improvement, depending upon the severity of the deficiency. (A written record of the oral reprimand should be maintained by the immediate supervisor.) 
(2)  Written reprimand. A department head may submit a written reprimand to an employee when oral warnings prove ineffective or when severe initial action is required. A copy shall be filed in the employee's personnel file. Included in the letter shall be a statement of the employee's right to appeal and appeal procedures. Two (2) reprimands within a twelve-month period for similar offenses may be grounds for dismissal. 
(3)  Suspension. A department head may, for disciplinary purposes, suspend without pay any employee in his department for a length of time that he considers appropriate, not to exceed ten (10) working days. However, the department head has the option of making an accumulated leave in lieu of suspending him without pay, and the department head may apply this equivalent deduction to all or part of the employee's suspension time. A written statement, specifically setting forth reasons for such suspension, shall be furnished to the affected employee by his department head, at the time of the suspension, and a copy filed with the human resources director. With the approval of the county administrator, an employee may be suspended for a longer period, pending the investigation or trial of criminal charges against him. However, the filing of criminal charges against an employee shall be evaluated to determine if there is a negative impact upon the county of sufficient magnitude to justify suspension. The fact that a person is acquitted of the charges or that the charges are dropped does not necessarily mean that the suspension or other disciplinary action will be revoked. 
(4)  Demotion. With the prior approval of the county administrator, a department head may reduce the salary of an employee or demote the employee, for cause. A written statement of the reasons for any such action shall be furnished to the affected employee, by his department head, on or before the effective date of the action, and a copy filed with the human resources director. 
(5)  Dismissals. Dismissals are separations made for delinquency, misconduct, inefficiency, inability to perform the work of the position satisfactorily, or conduct which seriously jeopardizes the health, welfare or safety of the county, its employees or the general public. 
(c)  Progressive discipline. The essential elements and responsibilities of progressive discipline are as follows: 
(1)  Department heads and employees shall be mutually responsible that all employees understand their assigned duties, rules, regulations, policies, and procedures which are applicable. 
(2)  Department heads shall be responsible for prompt and consistent enforcement of all applicable rules, regulations, policies, and procedures which are applicable. 
(3)  Department heads and employees shall be mutually responsible for understanding and following the principles of good employee relations. 
(4)  Department heads shall be responsible for proper documentation of all disciplinary actions taken. 
(d)  Reasons for disciplinary action. Listed below are some of the reasons which could be cause for disciplinary action referred to in subsection (a) above, but disciplinary action is not limited to the offenses listed: 
(1)  Being convicted of a crime for which a prison sentence is imposed. 
(2)  Too much lost time. 
(3)  Being absent without leave. 
(4)  Excessive tardiness or unapproved absences from work. 
(5)  Inefficiency. 
(6)  Abuse of county property. 
(7)  Willfully giving false statements to supervisors, officials, the public, or the board of commissioners. 
(8)  Violation of county administrative regulations or departmental rules, or public safety standard operating procedures. 
(9)  Drinking of alcoholic beverages while working, being intoxicated on the job, or using other than prescribed drugs while working. 
(10)  Discovery of a false statement in an application, which had not been detected previously, if such statement is of material evidence to the employee's current duties. 
(11)  Acceptance of gratuities in conflict with the policy outlined in section 10-33 of this chapter. 
(12)  Refusal to be examined by a physician designated by the county when so directed. 
(13)  Political activity in conflict with county policies. 
(14)  Borrowing county equipment for personal use. 
(15)  Conduct, on or off the job, unbecoming to a county employee, or conduct which brings discredit to the county, if the employee is provided with written specific incidents upon which the charge is based. 
(16)  Insubordination. 
(17)  Failure to perform the duties and responsibilities of his/her position at an acceptable level of competence. 
(e)  Dismissal, suspension, or demotion of department heads. The county administrator has the authority to dismiss, suspend, or demote a department head for cause in accordance with the guidelines outlined in subsection (b) of this section. 
(f)  Notice of disciplinary action. In all cases, the immediate supervisor shall notify the employee of the action taken and a copy of such notice will be retained in the employee's personnel file except in the case of a verbal reprimand. 
(g)  Appeal rights. A regular employee who is dismissed, suspended, or demoted shall be given written specific reasons for the action and advised of appeal rights in accordance with this section. 
(1)  Within five (5) work days of receipt of the written reasons for the action, the employee may counsel with the county administrator or his designee about the action. This meeting shall not include a representative of the employee nor other management representatives. 
(2)  The county administrator or his designee, or where applicable, the elected official or judicial official, shall give the employee a written response within five (5) work days of the meeting with the employee. This response will advise the employee of his rights to appeal to the board of commissioners. In the case of an employee working under the direction of an elected official or a judicial official, the right to appeal shall be with the appropriate elected official or a judicial official. Following that appeal to the appropriate elected official or judicial official, any further appeals shall be to the appropriate court of law with jurisdiction of the matter. 
(3)  A request for a hearing before the board of commissioners shall be submitted in writing to the county administrator or his designee within five (5) work days of receipt of the county administrator's response to the employee. 
(4)  The county administrator or his designee shall schedule the hearing as soon as practical after receipt of the request, but within fifteen (15) work days. 
(5)  The purpose of the hearing is for presentation of factual reasons for the action taken and for the employee to rebut these reasons and/or to show that the action taken was not justified. Either party may be represented by an attorney or other persons, but formal rules of evidence shall not be required. 
(6)  The chairman of the board of commissioners shall exercise full authority to restrict or prohibit testimony that is irrelevant to the original written reasons for the disciplinary action. 
(7)  The decision of the board of commissioners shall be by majority vote, taken in executive session, after the close of the hearing. Such decision shall be final. 
(8)  Either side may, at its own expense, provide for a written record of this hearing. The county administrator or his designee shall in any event provide stenographic assistance to record time and place of meeting, persons present and presenting testimony, the decision of the board of commissioners, and a written response to the employee within five (5) work days. 
(9)  The intent of time limits provided in this section is to provide for an expeditious settlement of appeals. A violation of these limits shall not prejudice the position of either party after a showing of reasonable cause for being unable to conform to the time limit. 
(10)  It shall be a violation of this policy for any member of county government to interfere, in any way, with disciplinary actions except following written appeals as provided herein. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. VII) 
Sec. 10-32. - Separations. 
(a)  Resignation. To resign in good standing, an employee must, in writing, give his department head at least fourteen (14) calendar days notice. Normally, failure to comply with this rule shall be entered on the service record of the employee and may result in a denial of reemployment rights. However, the department head, with the approval of the county administrator, may exempt from this penalty an employee who has given less than the required notice when exceptional circumstances warrant such exemption. 
All notices are final when accepted. Any employee who resigns and then wishes to return to work for the county shall be required to complete an application and must follow the same procedures as other applicants who are applying for the position under open, competitive appointments. 
(b)  Abandonment of position. An employee who, without valid reason, fails to report to work for three (3) consecutive days without authorized leave shall be separated from the payroll and reported as having abandoned his position. Such an employee is not eligible for reemployment. 
(c)  Layoffs. Any involuntary separation not involving delinquency, misconduct, inefficiency, or safety shall be considered a layoff. 
(1)  When, for any reason, it becomes necessary to reduce the working force in a department, regular employees shall be laid off on the basis of the following factors to be weighed equally: 
a.  Length of service in class. 
b.  Length of service with the county. 
c.  Average of performance ratings for the last three (3) years. 
(2)  When a department head believes that a certain individual is essential to the efficient operation of the department or organizational unit, because the individual possesses special skills or abilities and the department head wishes to retain this individual in preference to a person with a higher rating as provided above, the department head shall submit a written request to the county administrator for permission to do so. This request shall set forth, in detail, the specific skills and abilities possessed by the individual and the reasons why such individual is essential to the effective operation of the department. With the approval of the county administrator, the individual may be retained. 
(3)  If a regular employee is scheduled to be laid off, he may be offered a demotion to a lower class, if a vacancy exists and if he is qualified to fill positions in the lower class involved. 
(4)  Prior to a reduction in force, the names and job titles of all regular employees scheduled for layoff shall be submitted to the county administrator for approval, and until he has approved and confirmed the names submitted for layoff, no layoff shall be consummated. 
(5)  Regular employees to be laid off shall be notified, in writing, by the county administrator or his designee at least fourteen (14) calendar days prior to the effective date of the layoff. 
(6)  There shall be no appeal of separation by layoff, but the regular employee shall have the right of appeal if he believes these procedures have been improperly used. 
(d)  Disability. The county will comply with all state and federal statutes and regulations relating to the treatment of persons with disabilities. A department head may direct any employee under his jurisdiction to be examined by a physician designated by the county, and/or to provide a medical release for any existing pertinent medical records if the department head reasonably suspects that the employee is not able to perform the essential functions of the job. When a disability is discovered which impairs the effectiveness of a regular employee's job performance, or which makes their continuance on the job a danger to themselves or to others, the following action shall be taken: 
(1)  If the disability is correctable, the employee shall be allowed a specified time, as determined by the physician, to have it corrected. If they fail to take steps to have the disability corrected within this specified time, the employee shall be subject to disciplinary action or layoff. 
(2)  If, in the opinion of the examining physician, the disability cannot be corrected, the department head, subject to the approval of the county administrator, shall: Make reasonable accommodations to assist the employee to perform job duties. If reasonable accommodations cannot be made, the department head shall: Attempt to place the employee in another position which the employee can perform satisfactorily. If that cannot be accomplished successfully, the department head shall: Take steps to separate the employee from the county's service through retirement or layoff. 
(e)  Loss of job eligibility. Any employee who is unable to do their job adequately, because of loss of a necessary license or other requirement, shall be separated by a layoff. 
(f)  Dismissals. See section 10-31. 
(g)  Death. When a regular employee dies while in the service of the county, their estate shall be eligible to receive payment for their earned salary and accumulated annual leave. 
(h)  Effective date. The effective date of separation will be as listed below: 
(1)  Separations shall be effective on the last day of work. Accrued annual leave payment shall be calculated on that date, and no additional benefits shall accrue. 
(2)  Separation of an employee, who is unable to return to work for medical reasons, following use of all sick and annual leave or leave without pay, shall be effective on the last day of approved leave. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. VIII) 
Sec. 10-33. - Records and reports. 
(a)  Personnel transactions. All personnel records of employees of the county covered under these policies and all other records and materials relating to the administration of the career service personnel system shall be considered confidential and the property of the county. Information which is obtained in the course of official duties shall not be released by any employee other than by those charged with this responsibility as part of their official duties. Only that information which is required by federal and state law to be made available to the general public shall be released in cases when written request for such information is made to the human resources director. In all such cases, the employee shall be notified by the human resources director that a request to review information contained in the personnel records of the employee has been received. The employee shall have the opportunity to be present at any review of his personnel file by any member of the general public. 
All appointments, separations, and other personnel transactions shall be made on forms designated by the county administrator or his designee. 
Personnel files will be maintained in the human resources department and shall be confidential. Access is available only to: 
(1)  An employee. 
(2)  The supervisor or department head. 
(3)  The county administrator or his representative. 
(4)  Attorneys representing the county. 
(5)  Board of commissioners. 
Upon separation, a reference release form may be signed by the employee, indicating that reference information may be given to potential future employers. The employee may sign this form at his option. 
(b)  Public inspection. The following information relative to employees, and former employees, is available for public inspection at reasonable times and in accordance with such procedures as the county administrator or his designee may prescribe, such as: 
(1)  Name. 
(2)  Class. 
(3)  Title. 
(4)  Salary. 
(c)  Destruction of records. Employee service records shall be maintained according to state and federal standards after termination of employment. Such records may be kept, in their original form or in any other duplicate form that the human resources director deems appropriate. All other records, including correspondence, applications, and examinations may be destroyed after two (2) years. An employee data card, consisting of name, social security number, address, date of hire, date of termination, and rate of pay, will be maintained indefinitely. 
(d)  Attendance records. Regular attendance reports shall be prepared and submitted, by each department head, as requested by the county administrator and in the form designated by him. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. IX) 
Sec. 10-34. - Attendance and leave. 
(a)  Hours of work. The established work week and the hours of work shall, insofar as practicable, be uniform and shall be determined in accordance with the needs of the county and the reasonable needs of the public who may be required to do business with various county departments and with due regard to time commitments of staff outside usual office hours. The work schedule for each department shall be established by the department head with the approval of the county administrator. 
(b)  Lunch period. Lunch periods shall be scheduled in a manner to best serve the public. Employees are expected to utilize their lunch period during the hours designated by their supervisor. This time cannot be accumulated and can in no instance be saved for the purpose of leaving work early. 
(c)  Attendance. Each department head shall be responsible for the attendance of all persons in his or her department and shall keep complete attendance records including annual leave, sick leave, overtime, etc. Records of attendance shall be reported as provided in section 10-33. 
(d)  Holidays. The following days are designated as official holidays for employees in the career service: 
(1)  New Year's Day. 
(2)  Martin Luther King Day. 
(3)  Spring Holiday. 
(4)  National Memorial Day. 
(5)  Independence Day. 
(6)  Labor Day. 
(7)  Thanksgiving Day. 
(8)  Friday after Thanksgiving Day. 
(9)  Christmas Eve. 
(10)  Christmas Day. 
Whenever a holiday falls on Saturday, the preceding Friday shall be designated a substitute holiday and observed as the official holiday. When the holiday falls on Sunday, the following Monday shall be designated as the official holiday. An employee who is not on approved leave, and fails to report on his or her scheduled work day before or after a holiday, shall not be paid for the holiday. Holidays which occur during annual or sick leave shall not be charged against annual or sick leave. An employee who is required to work on a designated holiday will be afforded a day off in lieu of the holiday, to be taken within the next two (2) pay periods, and shall not accumulate compensatory time. 
(e)  Annual (vacation) leave. Vacations are for the purpose of rejuvenating both physical and mental faculties, and all employees are urged to avail themselves of vacation periods. The following rules shall apply to annual (vacation) leave: 
(1)  No employee shall receive pay, in lieu of vacation, unless recommendation is made by the county administrator and specific approval is given by the board. 
(2)  All full-time employees shall be entitled to earn and accrue annual (vacation) leave. Part-time and temporary employees shall not be eligible for annual leave. 
(3)  Full-time employees begin to accrue annual leave immediately upon employment. Employees under temporary appointment or provisional appointment, and employees not deemed to be in the career service, will not be granted annual leave under these policies. An employee in pay status for a full pay period during a calendar month earns annual leave for that month. 
(4)  Annual leave is accrued at the following rate: 
a.  One-half day per month for employees with 0—3 years of service; 
b.  One (1) day per month for employees with 4—9 years of service; 
c.  One and one-half days per month with 10 plus years of service. 
(5)  An employee reemployed, after a break in service, shall not receive annual accrual credits for previous service. 
(6)  A request for annual leave shall be submitted to the employee's immediate supervisor. Leave may be taken only after approval by the appropriate department head, so that, insofar as practicable, the department can function without the hiring of additional help. 
(7)  Unused annual leave, not to exceed thirty (30) days, may be carried into the next fiscal year. It is the intent of these rules to have employees take their annual leave yearly. 
(8)  When an employee is separated from service, he shall be paid for unused annual leave of up to maximum accrual. 
(f)  Sick leave. Sick leave shall be granted to an eligible employee for the following reasons: 
(1)  In the case of actual sickness or disability of the employee or for medical, dental, or eye examinations, maternity leave, or treatment for which arrangements cannot be made outside of working hours. 
(2)  When the employee is required to care for a sick or injured spouse, child, or parent or guardian. Sick leave also shall be granted when the employee is required to care for a sick or injured relative who is domiciled in the employee's household. The employee shall report his illness prior to his scheduled work time if possible. If not, he shall see that his illness is reported within thirty (30) minutes after the time he is scheduled to report to work. 
(3)  Those employees entitled to earn annual leave shall also be eligible to earn sick leave. 
(4)  Full-time employees begin to accrue sick leave, immediately upon employment, at the rate of one-half day per month. Part-time and temporary employees shall not be eligible for sick leave. 
(5)  A medical certificate signed by a licensed physician may be required by a department head to substantiate a request for sick leave for the following reasons: 
a.  Any period of absence consisting of three (3) or more consecutive working days. 
b.  To support a request for sick leave during a period when the employee is on vacation leave. 
c.  Leave of any duration, if absence from duty recurs frequently or habitually, provided the employee has been notified or warned that a certificate may be required. 
(6)  Unused sick leave, not to exceed forty-five (45) days, may be carried into the next fiscal year. This is the maximum allowable accumulation of sick leave. However, any eligible employee who has reached the maximum allowable accumulation of forty-five (45) days will be paid for the days earned but not taken during that fiscal year which exceed the forty-five (45) allowed days. 
(7)  No sick leave in excess of the leave accumulated to the employee's credit may be granted unless such sick leave advance is specifically authorized by the county administrator upon recommendation of the department head and the human resources director. 
(8)  A regular employee who separates from the county shall forfeit all unused sick leave. Such leave shall not be reinstated if the employee is rehired. 
(g)  Other types of leave. Listed below are the additional types of leave allowed by the county: 
(1)  Military leave. Military duty means training and service performed by an inductee, enlistee, reservist, or any entrant into a temporary component of the Armed Forces of the United States and time spent in reporting for and returning from such training in service. It also includes active duty training as a reservist in the Armed Forces of the United States or as a member of the National Guard of the United States. 
(2)  Jury duty. An employee shall be given necessary time off without loss of pay when performing jury duty with submission of evidence of actual days spent in court and with prompt return to work when dismissed from service or released by the court. An employee in good standing is also entitled to any court fees received in conjunction with jury duty. 
(3)  Civil leave. Any employee shall be given necessary time off, without the loss of pay, when performing emergency civilian duty in connection with national defense, when performing emergency duty with civil defense in connection with a natural disaster, or for the purpose of voting, when the polls are not open at least two (2) hours before or after an employee's scheduled hours of work. 
(4)  Funeral leave. In the event of death in an employee's immediate family, he or she will be granted paid funeral leave of three (3) scheduled work days. Any additional time taken will be without pay, or annual leave may be used. For the purpose of funeral leave, immediate family is defined as an employee's spouse, child or stepchild and their spouses, father, mother, father-in-law, mother-in-law, brother, sister, grandparents of the employee or of the employee's spouse, or any relative domiciled in the employee's household. For a brother-in-law or sister-in-law, funeral leave of one (1) day will be granted the day of the funeral. 
(5)  Workers' compensation and injury leave. The basic purpose of workers' compensation is to provide fixed benefits, according to the law, in the event an employee is injured or in an accident while in the course of employment. When injured, no matter how minor the injury, you should report it as promptly as possible to your supervisor. The employee will be on injury leave for a period of time to be determined by the doctor. The employee may request use of sick leave, and/or annual leave, to supplement workers' compensation benefits. 
(6)  Temporary disabilities not covered by workers' compensation. An employee who becomes temporarily disabled shall be allowed to exhaust his or her sick and vacation leave accumulations. After all sick and vacation leave have been used, further extension of leave, either with or without pay, must be specifically authorized by the county administrator, upon recommendation of the department head and the human resources director. 
(7)  Family and medical leave of absence without pay. Employees who have been employed for at least the preceding twelve (12) months and who worked at least one thousand two hundred fifty (1,250) hours during the preceding twelve (12) months are eligible for up to twelve (12) weeks of unpaid, job protected leave per year (calendar) in the following situations: 
a.  To care for a newborn child or a newly placed adopted or foster child; 
b.  To care for a seriously ill child, spouse, or parent; or 
c.  Because of the employee's own illness. 
Whenever possible, the county must be given at least thirty (30) days notice of the employee's intention to take leave prior to the date that the leave shall begin. If such notice is not possible, the employee must give as much notice as is practicable. The county reserves the right to require that any such medical leave be certified by the health care provider of the employee, child, spouse, or parent as indicated. Certification will be sufficient if it includes the date on which the illness commenced, the probable duration of the illness, all available appropriate medical facts, and where applicable, a statement that the employee is unable to perform his or her job or needed to care for his or her child, spouse, or parent. Any eligible employee who takes leave under this provision is entitled to return at the same position held prior to taking leave. Further, any benefits the employee had accrued prior to taking leave will be retained when the employee resumes working. Accumulated sick or annual leave is to be used as part of the twelve (12) weeks allowable under FMLA. Absences of one (1) week or more sick leave will be deducted from the FMLA allowance. 
(8)  Inclement weather leave. In the event of inclement weather, and transportation to the office is unsafe for employees, the county administrator may close the office. Employees will be notified of such closing by the news media. 
(9)  Absence without leave. An absence of an employee from duty, including any absence for a single day or part of a day, that is not authorized by a specific grant of leave of absence or as a work schedule variation under the provisions of these regulations, shall be deemed to be an absence without leave. Any such absence shall be without pay, and shall be cause for disciplinary action. 
(10)  Notification to human resources director. When an employee has taken leave of any kind, or is absent without leave, the department head shall notify the human resources director, in writing, within the same pay period in which the leave is taken or the absence without leave occurs. Such notification may be by notation on a time card or attendance sheet or by memo, giving specific information covering type of leave, dates and hours, and other pertinent data. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. X; Ord. of 12-19-06, § 1) 
Sec. 10-35. - Acceptance of gifts or gratuities; conflict of interest. 
(a)  Policy. It is the policy of the county that no employee shall accept gifts, gratuities, or loans from organizations, business concerns or individuals with whom he has official relationships, on business of the county. These limitations are not intended to prohibit the acceptance of articles, of negligible value, which are distributed generally, nor to prohibit employees from obtaining loans, from regular lending institutions, nor is it intended to preclude bona fide institutional fund-raising activities. 
It is particularly important that employees guard against relationships which might be construed as evidence of favoritism, coercion, unfair advantage, or collusion. No county employee, officer or agent shall participate in the selection, award or administration of a contract, if a conflict of interest, real or apparent, would be involved. 
(b)  Violations. Any violation of the above policy shall be communicated to the county administrator, and appropriate disciplinary action will be prescribed by the county administrator. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XI) 
Sec. 10-36. - Appeals and grievance procedures other than for disciplinary action. 
(a)  Policy. The most effective accomplishment of the work of the county requires prompt consideration and equitable adjustment of employee grievances. It is the desire of the county to adjust grievances informally, and both supervisors and employees are expected to make every effort to resolve problems as they arise. However, it is recognized that there will be grievances which will be resolved only after a formal appeal and review. 
The purpose of this rule is to insure that all employees are afforded fair, equitable, and expeditious review of their grievances without fear, coercion, or discrimination. 
(b)  Right of appeal. Any dispute between a supervisor and an employee concerning the interpretation of these policies may be appealed to the county administrator. If it is not satisfactorily resolved by the county administrator, it may be appealed to the board of commissioners, whose decision will be final. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XII) 
Sec. 10-37. - Outside employment. 
(a)  Rules. Outside employment is any paid employment, performed by an employee, in addition to his or her employment with the county. The following criteria will apply to outside employment: 
(1)  Such employment shall not interfere with the efficient performance of the employee's duties. 
(2)  Such employment shall not involve a conflict of interest or conflict with the employee's duties. 
(3)  Such employment shall not involve the performance of duties which the employee should perform as part of his or her employment with the county. 
(4)  Such employment shall not occur during the employee's regular or assigned working hours, unless the employee is on either annual leave, compensatory leave, or leave without pay. 
(5)  No employee, granted permission to engage in outside employment, shall work at such outside employment for a longer period of time than stated in his or her request for permission to engage in such employment. 
(6)  Any employee accepting outside employment under the terms of this rule shall make arrangements with the outside employer to be relieved from his or her outside duties, if and when called upon, for emergency service by the county. 
(7)  In public safety areas, additional criteria may be established to govern the number of hours which may be worked in outside employment due to safety concerns. 
(b)  Procedures. Any county employee desiring to perform outside employment shall first: 
(1)  File a request, in writing, with his or her department head for permission to engage in outside employment. The request shall state the type of employment and the hours of work, the name of the prospective employer, and the place where he is to be employed. 
(2)  The department head may either disapprove or recommend approval of the request. If the department head recommends approval, it may be granted by the county administrator or his designee if the criteria outlined above in subsection (a) are met. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XIII) 
Sec. 10-38. - Employment of relatives. 
(a)  Policy. The county may hire relatives of current employees if the new employee works in an entirely different department or location other than the current employee and does not work in a direct supervisor/employee relationship. Employees with the county at the time of the adoption of this policy are exempt from this provision. 
(b)  Exceptions. Exceptions to this policy should be rarely necessary and must be reviewed by the county administrator. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XIV) 
Sec. 10-39. - Political activity. 
(a)  Prohibition of political activity. No county employee shall: 
(1)  Use official authority or influence for the purpose of interfering with or affecting the result of an election or nomination for office. 
(2)  Directly or indirectly coerce, attempt to coerce, command or advise another employee to pay, lend or contribute anything of value to a party, committee, organization, agency or person for political purpose. 
(3)  Be a candidate for public or political party elective office, in a partisan primary, general or special election. 
(b)  Federal Hatch Act. The policies in subsection (a) are in accordance with provisions of the U.S. Code, §§ 1501 through 1508. Any employee who performs duties financed, in whole or in part, by federal loans or grants and/or who violates subsection (a) above is also in violation of federal law. 
(c)  Encouraged to vote. Everyone is entitled to his personal political opinion and is encouraged to exercise his right to vote. 
(d)  Nondiscrimination. No county employee shall be hired, promoted or favored or discriminated against with respect to employment because of his/her political opinions or affiliations. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XV) 
State Law reference— State department of public safety employees, political campaigns, O.C.G.A. § 35-2-12; nonelective state officers or employees holding office in political subdivision, political party, etc., O.C.G.A. § 45-10-70; coercion of other county officer, employee, etc., to make political contribution, O.C.G.A. § 45-11-10. 
Sec. 10-40. - Equal opportunity and nondiscrimination. 
(a)  Policy. There shall be no discrimination exercised due to race, national origin, color, religion, creed, age, handicap, sex, or political affiliation with respect to the recruiting and examination of applicants, the hiring of eligibles, or in any personnel transactions affecting employees, including training, promotion, separation and disciplinary actions. All personnel actions shall be based solely upon merit and fitness of the individual. 
(b)  Publicity. The county administrator shall see that information about job opportunities is readily available to potential job applicants. A continuing program shall be conducted to make the equal employment policies known to all citizens of the community and other potential job applicants. 
(c)  Appeals based on alleged discrimination. An applicant or employee who alleges discrimination in any personnel transaction shall have the right to appeal, as provided in section 10-31(g). 
(d)  Facilities accessible to the handicapped. The county will maintain offices in facilities that are accessible to the handicapped, or make any reasonable adjustments to office facilities, to eliminate architectural barriers to the handicapped. Any artificial barriers to employment will be eliminated. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XVI) 
Sec. 10-41. - Sexual harassment. 
The county adopted a sexual harassment policy on December 6, 1994. The terms and conditions of this policy shall be followed by all employees at all times. Please see the language contained in the sexual harassment policy for the procedures which should be followed in any case where allegations of sexual harassment are made. 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XVII) 
Sec. 10-42. - Categories of employment. 
(a)  Types of employees. Listed below are the different types of employees utilized by the county: 
(1)  Regular full-time employee; 
(2)  Regular part-time employee; 
(3)  Temporary employee; 
(4)  Nonexempt; 
(5)  Exempt. 
(b)  Work schedule. The work schedule of the county is listed below: 
(1)  Days and hours of work. The county's work week consists of forty (40) hours. However, the work week may vary for public safety positions. 
(2)  Work week of nonexempt staff. See above. 
(3)  Work week of exempt staff. Exempt employees' work schedules frequently will not coincide with the county's office hours. Exempt employees are expected to schedule their working hours, in consultation with their department head, to include evening meetings and activities outside the county's office hours. The annual salary of exempt employees is remuneration for the total responsibilities of their jobs. On those occasions where special meetings and activities, such as conferences and meetings that require weekend travel, etc., require an exempt employee working a substantial amount of overtime, some time may be given, with pay, to permit the individual to rest and care for personal matters. Such time shall always be given in close proximity to the period of overtime work and in an amount determined at the department head's discretion, after consultation with the county administrator or his designee. It must be used at once, with department head approval, and is not cumulative. 
The nature of many exempt jobs makes it impossible to confine the working schedule within usual office hours. It is the responsibility of both the employee and department head to plan irregular work schedules, when necessary, which permit accomplishment of all the regular duties of the job as designated by the county. The need to grant paid time off, due to excessive overtime, should arise only where special meetings and conferences outside the ongoing duties of the job require substantial additional hours of work. Distinction should be made between these special meetings and conferences and the schedule required by the usual duties of the job. 
An example of "substantial additional hours of work," which might warrant some time off, would be five (5) or more additional hours of work for four (4) consecutive weeks. The department head, after consulting with the county administrator or his designee, may grant one-half day of time off. Time off would be given immediately following the work period as stated above. 
When paid time off is granted to exempt employees, it is important that it be clear that it is not considered additional compensation for time worked, due to additional hours worked. It is to be given as a token of appreciation for the employee's effort and, consequently, bears no defined relationship to the number of hours of overtime worked. 
Frequent need for employees to work overtime, to complete their usual responsibilities, can be a signal to examine the work situation. Is the work load manageable? Is additional help needed? 
(Ord. of 12-19-95, Ch. XVIII) 
Secs. 10-43—10-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - SUBSTANCE ABUSE POLICY 

Sec. 10-61. - Policy established. 
The county is committed to providing a safe work environment and to fostering the well-being and health of its employees. That commitment is jeopardized when any county employee illegally uses drugs on or off the job, comes to work under their influence, possesses, distributes or sells drugs in the work place, or abuses alcohol on the job. Therefore, the county has established the following policy: 
(1)  It is a violation of county policy for any employee to use, possess, sell, trade, offer for sale, or offer to buy illegal drugs or otherwise engage in the illegal use of drugs on or off the job. 
(2)  It is a violation of company policy for any employee to report to work under the influence of or impaired by alcohol. 
(3)  It is a violation of the county policy for any employee to use prescription drugs illegally, i.e., to use prescription drugs that have not been legally obtained or in a manner or for a purpose other than as prescribed. (However, nothing in this policy precludes the appropriate use of legally prescribed medications.) 
(4)  Violations of this policy are subject to disciplinary action up to and including terminations. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Sec. 10-62. - Supervisors' responsibility. 
It is the responsibility of the county's supervisors to counsel employees whenever they see changes in performance or behavior that suggest an employee has a drug problem. Although it is not the supervisor's job to diagnose personal problems, the supervisor should encourage such employees to seek help and advise them about available resources for getting help. Everyone shares responsibility for maintaining a safe work environment, and coworkers should encourage anyone who has a drug problem to seek help. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Sec. 10-63. - Goal, intent. 
The goal of this policy is to balance our respect for individuals with the need to maintain a safe, productive and drug-free environment. The intent of this policy is to offer a helping hand to those who need it, while sending a clear message that the illegal use of drugs and the abuse of alcohol are incompatible with employment in the county. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Sec. 10-64. - Resource information. 
The county offers resource information on various means of employee assistance in the community, including but not limited to drug and alcohol abuse programs. Employees are encouraged to use this resource file, which is located in the human resources department in the county administration building. In addition, the county will distribute this information to employees for their confidential use. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Sec. 10-65. - General procedures. 
(a)  An employee reporting to work visibly impaired will be deemed unable to properly perform required duties and will not be allowed to work. If possible, the employee's supervisor will first seek another supervisor's opinion to confirm the employee's status. Next, the supervisor will consult privately with the employee to determine the cause of the observation, including whether substance abuse has occurred. If, in the opinion of the supervisor, the employee is considered impaired, the employee will be sent home or to a medical facility by taxi or other safe transportation alternative, depending on the determination of the observed impairment, and accompanied by the supervisor or another employee if necessary. A drug test may be in order. An impaired employee will not be allowed to drive. 
(b)  Employees and job applicants who have a positive confirmed test result may explain or contest the result to the county within five (5) working days after the county contacts the employee or job applicant and shows him/her the positive test result as it was received from the laboratory in writing. 
(c)  The confidentiality of any information received by the employer through a substance abuse testing program shall be maintained, except as otherwise provided by law. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Sec. 10-66. - Job applicant testing. 
(a)  All job applicants at the county will undergo testing for the presence of illegal drugs as a condition of employment. Any applicant with a confirmed positive test will be denied employment. 
(b)  Applicants will be required to submit voluntarily to a urinalysis test at a laboratory chosen by the county, and by signing a consent agreement will release the county from liability. 
(c)  If the physician, official or lab personnel has reasonable suspicion to believe that the job applicant has tampered with the specimen, the applicant will not be considered for employment. 
(d)  The county will not discriminate against applicants for employment because of a past history of drug abuse. It is the current abuse of drugs, preventing employees from performing their jobs properly, that the county will not tolerate. 
(e)  Individuals who have failed a preemployment test may initiate another inquiry with the county after a period of not shorter than six (6) months; but they must present themselves drug-free as demonstrated by urinalysis or other test selected by the county. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Sec. 10-67. - Notification to county of criminal violation. 
As a condition of employment, employees must abide by the terms of this policy and must notify the county in writing of any conviction of a violation of a criminal drug statute occurring in the workplace no later than five (5) calendar days after such conviction. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Sec. 10-68. - Employee testing. 
(a)  The county has adopted testing practices to identify employees who use illegal drugs on or off the job. It shall be a condition of employment for all employees to submit to drug testing under the following circumstances: 
(1)  When there is reasonable suspicion to believe that an employee is using illegal drugs. The following circumstances could cause reasonable suspicion: 
a.  Observed drug use. 
b.  Abnormal conduct or erratic behavior. 
c.  Apparent physical state of impairment. 
d.  Accidents or other actions that provide reasonable cause to believe the employee may be under the influence of drugs. 
e.  Evidence that an employee has used, possessed, sold, solicited, or transferred drugs while working or while on the county's premises or while operating the county's vehicle, machinery or equipment. 
f.  Evidence that an individual has tampered with any substance abuse test during his or her employment with the county. 
(2)  When employees have caused or contributed to an on-the-job injury that resulted in a loss of work time, which means any period of time during which an employee stops performing the normal duties of employment and leaves the place of employment to seek care from a licensed medical provider. The county may send employees for a substance abuse test if they are involved in on-the-job accidents where personal injury or damage to county property occurs. 
(3)  As part of a followup program to treatment for drug abuse. 
(4)  When a substance abuse test is conducted as part of a routinely scheduled employee fitness-for-duty medical examination that is part of the county's established policy or that is scheduled routinely for all members of an employment classification or group. 
(b)  Employees with a confirmed positive test result may, at their option and expense, have a second confirmation test made on the same specimen. An employee will not be allowed to submit another specimen for testing. 
(c)  If the physician, official or lab personnel has reasonable suspicion to believe that the employee has tampered with the specimen, the employee is subject to disciplinary action up to and including termination. 
(Ord. of 4-16-96) 
Secs. 10-69—10-79. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - WORKERS' COMPENSATION RETURN TO WORK POLICY 

Sec. 10-80. - Policy established. 
It is the policy of Gordon County to provide and establish a return to work policy and procedure for employees with work-related injuries and illnesses who are unable, temporarily and permanently, to return to their permanent job duties. 
Because Gordon County recognizes that their employees are a valued and limited resource, this program is designed to: 
(a)  Assist the medical recovery process by providing a focus and a goal for return of the injured employee. 
(b)  Benefit employees by allowing them to return to full wages as soon as possible. 
(c)  Benefit employer by reducing workers' compensation costs. 
The workers' compensation return to work policy will be adopted and added to the Gordon County Safety Ordinance. 
(Mo. of 8-20-02) 
Chapter 11 - PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT[1] 
Footnotes:

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 11-1. - Designation as redevelopment area. 
The county is hereby designated as a redevelopment area under the provisions of the Public Works and Economic Development Act of 1965, as amended, and further the District O.E.D.P. is adopted as the county plan, in lieu of submitting an area O.E.D.P. for the county. 
(Res. of 1-4-77) 
Sec. 11-2. - Development authority. 
(a)  There is hereby determined and declared to be a pressing, existing and future need for a development authority, as more fully described and defined in the Development Authorities Law (O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq.), to function in the county, for the purpose of developing and promoting for the public good and general welfare trade, commerce, industry and employment opportunities in the county and thereby promoting the general welfare of the state. 
(b)  There is hereby activated in the county the public body corporate and politic known as the "Development Authority of Gordon County" which was created upon the adoption and approval of the Development Authorities Law (O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq.) and particularly O.C.G.A. § 36-62-4. 
(c)  The board of directors appointed as provided by law shall organize itself, carry out its duties and responsibilities and exercise its powers and prerogatives in accordance with the terms and provisions of the Development Authorities Law (O.C.G.A. § 36-62-1 et seq.) as it now exists and as it may hereafter be amended or modified. 
(d)  At the end of any term of office of any director, a successor thereto shall be so appointed. 
(Res. of 4-24-75)

ARTICLE VIII. - HISTORIC PRESERVATION 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 11-387. - Purposes of historic preservation commission. 
(a)  To support and further the belief that the Civil War and other historical, cultural and aesthetic heritage of Gordon County, Georgia are among its most valued and important assets, and that the preservation of this heritage is essential to the promotion of the health, education, prosperity, and general welfare of the people; 
(b)  To protect and enhance local Civil War, historical, and aesthetic attractions to tourists and thereby promote and stimulate the business environment within Gordon County; 
(c)  To enhance all opportunities for federal or state tax benefits pursuant to relevant provisions of federal or state law; 
(d)  To provide for the designation, protection, preservation, and rehabilitation of historic properties and historic districts, and to participate in federal, state, local, or private programs to do the same.
